In children during autumn and summer, many experience heat vomiting, characterized by the expulsion of yellow phlegm, a warm forehead, a feeling of heat in the five palms, and possibly infrequent and reddish urination—this is termed heat vomiting. If there is dry retching without material, it is advisable to administer Xiangru drink.

Heat vomiting in children arises from excessive consumption of sweet and roasted foods, or from the rich flavors of a wet nurse's diet, leading to heat accumulation in the stomach, or due to heat from the summer sun penetrating the stomach. If there are muscle spasms and symptoms of restlessness and thirst, it indicates that summer heat has harmed the stomach's energy; first, use Xiangru powder, and then bamboo shavings soup.

If the vomit is yellowish and the child cannot accept anything, it indicates heat in the stomach; start with a yellow purging powder, followed by ginseng stomach-soothing powder. If the expulsion is sour and foul, it is caused by food stagnation; use Baohe pills. If there is vomiting of undigested milk, it signifies weak stomach energy; administer Yigong powder.

If vomiting is accompanied by reduced appetite and abdominal pain with a desire for pressure, it points to spleen qi deficiency; use Liu Junzi powder with added wood fragrance.

Overall, it is essential to examine the fingers; if they are warm, it indicates stomach heat, while if cool, it indicates stomach cold. For heat, use yellow purging powder; for cold, use warming middle soup; if neither hot nor cold, aim to balance with Yigong powder.[45p]

　　　　　毒气吐
　　巢氏云：春夏以汤与儿，肠胃脆弱，不胜药势，遂吐下不止，药熏脏腑，烦恼顿乏，为中毒气吐下。
　　　　　伤乳吐

　　乳下婴儿乳哺太过，或儿睡着而更口　衔乳，岂有厌足，以致脾不能运，胃不能受，满而溢，故令呕吐。长此不已，遂致慢惊，可不慎乎？此候但令节乳为上，甚者宜暂断乳，先令乳母服调气之剂，儿服消乳丸，化乳消食为上。若吐自口角出，即是乳多不能消化满溢之证，非病也，不可妄投他洽吐药。凡吐乳直出而不停留者，谓之哯乳，但以炒麦芽三钱，橘红一钱，丁香三分，水煎服之，立止。[46p]

Poisonous Gas Vomiting

Chao Shi states: In spring and summer, when a child is given soup, their intestines and stomach are weak and cannot withstand medicinal effects, leading to continuous vomiting and diarrhea. The medicine steams the organs, causing distress and fatigue, resulting in poisoning from gas causing vomiting and diarrhea.

Injurious Milk Vomiting

When an infant breastfeeds excessively, or if the child falls asleep while still nursing, there is no sense of fullness, leading to the spleen’s inability to function and the stomach’s inability to retain, causing fullness and overflow, hence inducing vomiting. If this continues, it can lead to chronic shock. Caution is advised! In this situation, it is best to regulate breastfeeding. If severe, one should temporarily stop breastfeeding, allowing the nurse to take a soothing formula and the child to take breast-milk dissolving pills to convert milk into digestible food. If vomiting occurs directly from the mouth corners, it indicates that the milk is excessive and cannot be digested, resulting in overflow; this is not a disease, and one should not rashly administer other vomiting medications. Vomiting milk that comes out directly without remaining is termed "regurgitated milk." To stop it, decoct three qian of roasted barley, one qian of dried tangerine peel, and three fen of clove in water to be taken; this will stop the vomiting immediately.[46p]

　　　　　泻

　　论泻之源，有冷泻、热泻、伤食泻、水泻、积泻、惊泻、风泻、脏寒泻、疳积酿泻，种种不同，各分于后：　　冷泻：多是白水，泻密而少，腹痛而鸣，眉皱目慢，面带白色，额有汗，多用冲和饮，当归散合和，水煨姜煎服，并守中汤、参苓白朮散、益中膏、沉香槟榔丸治之。　　热泻：大便黄色，如筒吊水，泻过即止，半日复然，心烦口渴，小便黄少，食乳必粗，先用五苓散或大顺饮，次以钱氏白朮散主之；香薷散亦佳。　　伤食泻：乃脾胃素弱，复为生冷果食所伤，故大便不聚而泻；或因乳母餐生冷肥腻之物，自乳而过，亦能作泻。面唇俱白，泻稀而少，或如坏鸡子，腥臭异常，身形黄瘦，宜先温正胃气，次理积而后固脾，冲和饮、当归散合和，煨姜、枣子煎服。理积，儿大者乌犀丸，小者化癖丸、三棱散；固脾，和中散、醒脾散。[47p]

Diarrhea

Regarding the causes of diarrhea, there are various types: cold diarrhea, hot diarrhea, food-related diarrhea, watery diarrhea, accumulation diarrhea, shock diarrhea, wind diarrhea, visceral cold diarrhea, and malnutrition-induced diarrhea. Each has its own characteristics, described as follows:

Cold Diarrhea: Often characterized by clear watery stools, infrequent bowel movements, abdominal pain accompanied by sounds, a furrowed brow, slow eye movements, a pale face, sweating on the forehead, and is often treated with warming herbal drinks, a mixture of Angelica powder, ginger decoction, and remedies such as Zhong Tang, Shen Ling Bai Zhu San, Yi Zhong Gao, and Chen Xiang Bing Lang Wan.

Hot Diarrhea: The stool is yellow, similar to water pouring from a tube; it stops after a bout, but reappears after half a day. Symptoms include irritability, thirst, and scant yellow urine. Foods consumed are often coarse. Initial treatments include Wu Ling San or Da Shun Yin, followed by Qian’s Bai Zhu San; Xiang Ru San is also effective.

Food-Related Diarrhea: This arises from a weak spleen and stomach, further aggravated by raw and cold fruits, causing loose stools; it may also derive from nursing mothers consuming raw, cold, and greasy foods which then adversely affect the child. Symptoms include pale lips and face, watery and less stool, sometimes with an abnormal foul smell, and yellowed thin appearance. The initial treatment focuses on warming and regulating the stomach's Qi, followed by addressing accumulations to solidify the spleen. Suitable remedies include Chōng Hé Yǐn, a mixture of Angelica powder, ginger, and dates decoction. For accumulation, larger children may take Wū Xī Wán, while smaller children might use Huà Pí Wán or Sān Lǐng Sàn; to solidify the spleen, methods include Hé Zhōng Sàn and Xǐng Pí Sàn.[47p]

　　水泻谓之洞泄，乃阴阳不顺，水壳不分，泻黄水而小便少，番次密而无度。是夏秋之际，昼则解衣取凉，夜则失盖感冷，冷热相激，清浊浑乱；或因母自热中来，乳有热气，遽以哺之，令儿脾胃不和，水壳交杂而下，以(口父)咀五苓散加薏苡仁、车前子、半夏，水、姜煎服，分正阴阳；或先用大顺饮、温白汤、调下香薷散，调中止补。钱氏白朮散、六和汤亦好。　　积泻：脾气虚弱，乳食入胃，不能运化，积滞日久，再为冷食所伤，传之大肠，遂成泄泻，留连不止，诸药无效。盖以积在脾胃，积既未除，何由得愈？宜先除积，后止泻，泻止实脾则病除矣。三棱散、乌犀丸，续用沉香槟榔丸、参苓白朮散、和中散、香橘饼调理。　　惊泻：粪青如苔，稠若胶粘，不可便止，但镇心抑肝，和脾胃，消乳食，斯为治法。先投五苓散，次用三棱散，水姜、仓米煎服。[48p]

Diarrhea is termed "dòng xiè" (洞泄), which arises from an imbalance of yin and yang, where the body's fluids are not properly separated. This results in yellow water being expelled with little urine produced, and the discharges become frequent and excessive. This typically occurs between summer and autumn when, during the day, one may shed clothing for relief from heat, and at night, the loss of coverings causes a feeling of cold. The clash of hot and cold leads to confusion of the clear and turbid. Additionally, it may stem from a nursing mother having internal heat, which transfers heat to the milk. If the child is abruptly fed, it causes a discord in the child's spleen and stomach, mixing and expelling the fluids. In this case, one might use Wuling Powder combined with Coix seeds, Plantago seeds, and Pinellia, boiled in water with ginger, to correct the imbalance of yin and yang. Alternatively, one could start with Dashun Drink, warm white soup, or Xiangru Powder to regulate and mitigate the condition. Qian's Bai Zhu Powder and Liu He Soup are also effective.

Accumulated diarrhea occurs due to a weakness in the spleen's qi, where milk and food enter the stomach but cannot be properly metabolized, leading to stagnation over time. If cold foods further harm the stomach, the condition may progress to diarrhea that persists without end, rendering various medicines ineffective. Since the condition remains in the spleen and stomach, it cannot be cured until the accumulation is removed. Therefore, one should first eliminate the accumulation before addressing the diarrhea itself; once the diarrhea stops and the spleen is fortified, the illness will resolve. Treatments such as Sanleng Powder and Wuxi Pill can be applied, followed by the use of Chenxiang Betel Nut Pill, Shenling Baizhu Powder, Hezhong Powder, and Xiangju Cake for recovery.

In cases of shock-induced diarrhea, the stool is dark green and sticky like glue, and one should not hastily stop it. Rather, the focus should be on calming the heart, soothing the liver, and harmonizing the spleen and stomach to digest the breast milk and food. The treatment involves first administering Wuling Powder, followed by Sanleng Powder, brewed with water and ginger, and served with barnyard millet.[48p]

或三解散，神曲生姜煎汤调服，及沉香槟榔丸、不惊丹调治。　　风泻：慢惊大病后有之，其粪稀黄褐色，或夹食不消，乳食同下，此因脾虚所致，或夹黑褐色者，属肾，盖脾虚为肾水所乘故也。若久不进饮食，再有惊搐，宜疏肾水、去脾风，次补脾则自愈，庶无复作之患。疏肾水，(口父)咀五苓散加黑牵牛半生半炒，并薏苡仁，水、姜煎服。去脾风，泻黄散。调脾气，参苓白朮散。　　脏寒泻：粪如青竹色，不稀不稠，或下青水，未泻时腹痛而鸣，叫哭方泻，多是生来三五月内有此，周岁则无。始因断脐带短，风冷自外逼内，而成此疾。先用冲和饮、水、葱白煎投，温中解表；次以当归散，水、煨姜煎服，及投匀气散、理中汤。[49p]

If there is a sudden scattering, administer a mixture of ginger decoction with Shenqu (divine music) and take Chénxiāng (sandalwood), Bīngláng (betel nut) pills, and Wujingdan (non-surprising elixir).

Regarding wind diarrhea: This occurs after a major shock or illness, with loose stools that are yellow-brown, possibly mixed with undigested food, similar to milk food. This is due to spleen deficiency. If there are dark brown stools, it relates to kidney issues, as spleen deficiency allows kidney water to overwhelm it. If one does not consume food for a long time and experiences additional shock or convulsions, one should promote kidney water flow and eliminate spleen wind, then replenish the spleen for self-healing, thus preventing recurrence. To promote kidney water, take Wǔlíngsǎn (Five-ingredient powder) with half raw and half roasted Qianniuzi, along with job’s tears in water and ginger decoction. To eliminate spleen wind, take Xièhuángsǎn (Yellow-reducing powder). To regulate spleen energy, use Shēn-líng-bái-zhú-sǎn (Ginseng, Poria and Atractylodes powder).

For organ cold diarrhea: The stools resemble the color of green bamboo, neither too loose nor too firm, or may present as greenish water. Before the diarrhea, there might be abdominal pain and sounds, often accompanied by crying just before defecation. This typically occurs within the first three to five months of life and does not extend beyond the first year. The initial cause stems from a short umbilical cord, with wind and cold forcing in from outside, resulting in this ailment. Initially, use a soothing drink with water and white scallion decoction to warm the center and resolve the exterior; followed by taking Dāngguīsǎn (Angelica powder), water, and roasted ginger decoction, as well as a blend of Qi regulators and Lǐzhōngtāng (Regulating the center decoction).[49p]

　　疳积酿泻：其候面色萎黄，腹胀脚弱，头大项小，发稀且竖，肌肉消瘦，不思饮食，昼凉夜热，或腹内有症癖气块，泻则颜色不等，其臭异常，其泻有时，或一月、半月、旬日一番，自泻自止，名为疳积酿泻。先以当归散加三棱、陈皮，水、姜煎服；次投乌犀丸、沉香槟榔丸，及化癖丸、芦荟丸、没石子丸。儿最小者难下丸子，止投三棱散、快膈汤，目然痊愈。[50p]

Parasitic accumulation leading to diarrhea: The symptoms include a pale yellow complexion, abdominal distension, weak legs, a large head with a small neck, sparse and upright hair, emaciated muscles, a lack of appetite, cool during the day and hot at night, and possibly gas or lumps in the abdomen. The diarrhea is of inconsistent color and has an unusual odor, occurring intermittently, which may happen every month, half-month, or every ten days, with spontaneous onset and resolution, referred to as parasitic accumulation leading to diarrhea. First, administer a decoction of Angelica powder combined with Poria and dried tangerine peel; next, use black rhinoceros pill, agarwood betel nut pill, as well as obstruction relief pill, aloe pill, and myrrh pill. For the youngest children, who have difficulty taking pills, only administer the Poria powder and quick relief soup, which can lead to noticeable recovery.[50p]

　　若泻或痢，青色甚而淡黄夹白，寒多热少，此阴邪胜阳，宜用守中汤、胃苓汤与服，扶表救里，方进当归散加陈皮、紫苏，水，姜、糯米煎服；亦宜和解，理中汤，清米饮空心调服，温脾去湿，益气清神。寒盛者，理中汤内加熟附子，水、姜、枣煎服；次投南星腹皮饮，水、姜煎服，和脾胃，去阴邪。　　若泻或泄色青淡而有沫黄稠，热多寒少，亦致面黄肌瘦，烦躁不宁，宜以(口父)咀五苓散加薏苡仁、车前子，水、姜煎服；解散余邪，仍用茵陈蒿、栀子仁煎汤，调细末五苓散温服，退黄色，消阳毒；及当归散，水、姜、枣煎投，或服万安饮、四神丸。[51p]

If there is diarrhea or dysentery, with a blue color and pale yellow mixed with white, cold predominating over heat, this indicates that the yin evil overcomes the yang. It is advisable to use Shou Zhong Decoction and Wei Ling Decoction, to support the exterior and rescue the interior. Additionally, the formula Dang Gui San can be combined with Chen Pi and Zi Su, boiled with water, ginger, and glutinous rice; it is also beneficial to harmonize and resolve with Li Zhong Decoction, and drink Qing Mi Yin on an empty stomach to warm the spleen, eliminate dampness, tonify qi, and clear the spirit. If there is excessive cold, add熟附子 to Li Zhong Decoction, and boil with water, ginger, and dates for consumption; next, administer Nan Xing Fu Pi Decoction, boiled with water and ginger, to harmonize the spleen and stomach and eliminate yin evil.

If there is diarrhea and the color is blue and pale with thick yellow foam, with heat predominating over cold, this can also result in a yellow face and emaciated body, restlessness and unease. It is advisable to use Wu Ling San (adjusted) with added Yi Yi Ren and Che Qian Zi, boiled with water and ginger for consumption; this disperses residual evil. Additionally, use Yin Chen Hao and Zhi Zi Ren in a decoction, mix with fine powder of Wu Ling San for warm consumption, to reduce yellowishness and dispel yang toxins; and also administer Dang Gui San, boiled with water, ginger, and dates, or take Wan An Drink and Si Shen Wan.[51p]

　　　　　冷泻

　　汤氏云：冷泻者，乃脾胃虚寒。水壳不化而泄。钱仲阳云：小儿不能食乳，泻褐色，身冷，无阳也，当用益黄散加减治之。大便青白，口不烦渴，冷积泻也，理中汤主之。若口鼻吸风寒之气，脾胃受生冷之食而作者，先用理中汤，后用异功散。命门火衰，不能温蒸中州之气，故脾胃虚寒者用益黄散及八味丸，脾胃虚弱者五味异功散，脾气下陷者补中益气汤，脾气虚寒者人参理中汤，寒水侮土者益黄散，肝木乘脾者四君柴胡散，手足并冷者加木香、干姜，治者审之！　　丹溪云：泻青亦是寒，宜用苏合香丸、平胃散各等分，蜜汤调服。　　田氏云：便青者，因惊风内藏，脾气不和，宜白朮汤。[52p]

Cold Diarrhea

Tang stated: Cold diarrhea arises from deficiency and coldness of the spleen and stomach. Water fails to transform and therefore leads to diarrhea. Qian Zhongyang said: If a child is unable to consume milk, has brown diarrhea, and feels cold with no warmth in the body, one should use a modified version of the Yi Huang San. If the stools are bluish-white, and there is no thirst or impatience, it is cold accumulation diarrhea, and should be treated with Li Zhong Tang. If one is exposed to wind-cold air through the mouth and nose, and the spleen and stomach are affected by cold food, first use Li Zhong Tang, followed by Yi Gong San. When the fire of the Mingmen is weak, it cannot warm the qi of the Middle Jiao; therefore, those with cold deficiency of the spleen and stomach should use Yi Huang San and Ba Wei Wan. For individuals with weak spleen and stomach, use Wu Wei Yi Gong San; for those with sinking spleen qi, use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang; for cold and water harming the earth, apply Yi Huang San; when liver wood overacts on the spleen, use Si Jun Chai Hu San; and for cold extremities, add Mu Xiang and Gan Jiang. The practitioner should be discerning!

Danxi stated: Blue diarrhea is also due to cold, and it is advisable to use Su He Xiang Wan and Ping Wei San in equal parts, mixed with honeyed water for administration.

Tian stated: The bluish stools are due to fright wind affecting the interior and disharmony of spleen qi; therefore, Bai Zhu Tang is appropriate.[52p]

　　　　　热泻

　　薛氏云：右腮色赤，饮冷，胃经实热也，用泻黄散。恶冷喜热，胃经虚热也，用白朮散。右腮及额间俱赤，心脾热也，用泻黄散加炒黑黄连。若左颊左腮俱赤，肝火乘脾土也，用四君子汤加柴胡。若儿暴伤乳食，用保和丸；乳母尤当忌厚味，节饮食。若乳母停食所伤，致儿吐泻等病，当治其母。大抵始病而热者，邪气胜则实也；终变为寒者，真气夺则虚也。久病而热者，内其寒而外假热也。久泻元气虚寒，当参前证治之。
　　　　　伤食泻

　　东垣云：伤食则恶食。小儿食泻者，因饮食伤脾，脾气不能健运，故乳食不化而出。若嗳臭吞酸，胸膈胀满腹痛，按之益痛者，虽作泻而所停滞之物尚未消也，用保和丸。腹痛按之不痛者，乳食已消也，用异功散。脾气伤而未复，不思饮食者，用六君子汤。所伤生冷之物及喜热者，并加木香、干姜。乳食已消，腹痛已止，泻尚未止者，脾失清升之气也，用补中益气汤。余有别证，当参各门。[53p]

Heat Diarrhea

Xue said: If the right cheek is red and the person drinks cold water, it indicates excess heat in the stomach; use the Xie Huang San. If the person dislikes cold and prefers heat, it indicates deficiency heat in the stomach; use the Bai Zhu San. If both the right cheek and forehead are red, it suggests heart and spleen heat; use Xie Huang San with fried black Huang Lian. If the left cheek and left side of the face are both red, it indicates liver fire affecting the spleen; use Si Jun Zi Tang with Chai Hu. If a child suffers from dietary injury, use Bao He Wan; nursing mothers should especially avoid rich foods and regulate their diet. If a nursing mother’s diet leads to her child’s vomiting and diarrhea, the treatment should focus on the mother. Generally, if heat appears at the onset of illness, it is due to prevailing evil qi, indicating excess; if it transforms to cold at the end, it shows true qi being depleted, indicating deficiency. Prolonged illness with heat indicates internal cold masked by false heat. Prolonged diarrhea with depletion of original qi requires reference to previous treatments.

Food Injury Diarrhea

Dong Yuan said: In cases of food injury, there is a dislike for food. For children experiencing diarrhea due to dietary issues, the spleen is harmed, and its qi cannot function properly, resulting in undigested dairy and food. If there is foul belching and sourness, with a sensation of fullness or pain in the chest and abdomen that worsens when pressed, it indicates that the stagnant matter has not yet resolved, and Bao He Wan should be used. If abdominal pain does not worsen when pressed, it indicates that the dairy and food have been digested; use Yi Gong San. If spleen qi is damaged and there is a lack of appetite, use Liu Jun Zi Tang. For injuries from cold foods or a preference for warmth, add Mu Xiang and Gan Jiang. If dairy and food have been digested and abdominal pain has stopped, but the diarrhea persists, it indicates a loss of the spleen's rising clear qi; use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang. Other specific conditions should be addressed according to their respective categories.[53p]

　　钱氏云：黄承务子二岁，病伤食而泻，众医与止之，十余日，便青白，乳食不消，身凉加哽气昏睡，咸谓困笃，召钱。钱先与益黄散、补肺散各三服，三日身温而不哽气，后以白饼子微下之，又与益脾散三服利止。何以然？利本脾虚伤食，初不与下之，留连十日，上实下虚，脾气弱则引肺亦虚，脾肺子母故也。今先补脾则肺病自退，即身温不哽气也。然后下其所伤。或曰：何不先下后补？曰：便青为下脏冷，若先下必大虚，今先实脾而后下则不虚矣。后更与补之，乃安。[54p]

Qian said: When Huang Chengwu was two years old, he fell ill, suffering from poor appetite and diarrhea. Many doctors attempted to stop it, but after more than ten days, he became pale and weak, his milk and food were not digesting, his body felt cold, and he was troubled by a feeling of heaviness and drowsiness. They all believed he was in a severe state and called for Qian.

Qian first gave him three doses each of Yihuang Powder and Pulmonary Nourishing Powder. After three days, his body warmed up, and he no longer had the feeling of heaviness. Then, with a small amount of white rice porridge, he introduced another three doses of Spleen Nourishing Powder to stimulate recovery and stop the discomfort.

Why did he do this? The diarrhea stemmed from a deficiency in the spleen due to improper eating. Initially, he did not administer purgatives because of the prolonged retention. After ten days, the upper system was full while the lower was weak. A weak spleen qi draws the lungs into weakness, as they are interdependent like mother and child. By first nourishing the spleen, the lung condition naturally recedes, which is why his body warmed up and the heaviness disappeared. Then, only did he address the cause of his injury.

Someone asked: Why not purge first and then nourish? He replied: The paleness indicates the lower organs are cold. If we purged first, it would lead to significant weakness. Now, by first fortifying the spleen and then purging, there would be no weakness. After this, he provided further nourishment, which ultimately restored his well-being.[54p]

　　　　　惊泻

　　仲阳云：慢惊病后，或吐泻胃虚，或气弱因惊。眼白如淡墨，下粪青黄，此泻合温补，至圣保命丹、钓藤饮主之。或乳随粪下，消乳丸、进食丸主之。或微渴，心脾喘燥狂热，此泻尤难治，辰砂五苓散主之。冷者定命饮子治之。后与温惊朱君散、睡惊太乙丹。　　小儿惊泻者，肝主惊，肝木也，盛则必传克于脾，脾土既衰，则乳食不化，水道不调，故泄泻色青，或兼发搐者，盖青乃肝之色，搐乃肝之证也。亦有因乳母脾虚受惊，及怒动肝火而致者。经曰：怒则气逆，甚则呕血及飧泄，法当平肝补脾，慎勿用峻攻之药。脾气益虚，肝邪弥甚，甚则抽搐反张者，亦肝火炽盛，中州亏损之变证也。凡见惊证，只宜用四君、六君、异功散等方，加白附子定风，柴胡平肝，引经以杜渐，则必不致泻搐而自安矣。今已见吐泻惊搐，尚不知补脾平肝，以保命、抱龙、镇惊等药治之，其亦去生远矣。[55p]

Shock-related Diarrhea

Zhong Yang states: After a shock, one may experience vomiting and diarrhea due to a weakened stomach, or a deficiency of qi due to emotional distress. If the sclera appears pale and the stool is greenish-yellow, this diarrhea requires warming and supplementation; use the Sacred Life Preservation Pill or the Diaoteng Decoction for treatment. If milk is accompanied by diarrhea, use the Milk Dissolving Pill or Food Intake Pill. For mild thirst, heart and spleen symptoms manifesting as irritability and fever, this type of diarrhea is particularly difficult to treat; use the Cinnabar and Five Poria Powder. In cases of severe cold, the Definitive Life-preserving Decoction should be used. Later, administer the Warm Shock Red Monarch Powder or the Sleeping Shock Celestial Medicine.

For children with shock-related diarrhea, the liver governs emotional distress. When the liver is excessive, it must transmit to the spleen. When the spleen is weakened, it fails to properly digest food, resulting in unregulated water passage, hence the greenish color of the diarrhea. If there are also convulsions, the green color indicates liver issues and convulsions indicate liver symptoms. There are also cases where the lactating mother suffers from spleen deficiency due to shock, leading to anger and liver fire. The treatise states: anger causes qi to rebel; if severe, it results in vomiting blood and food-related diarrhea. Thus, the method should focus on soothing the liver and supplementing the spleen; one must be cautious not to use harsh purgatives. If the spleen qi becomes increasingly deficient and liver evils worsen, serious cases involving convulsions and rigidity also signify intense liver fire and exhaustion of the Central Qi.

Whenever signs of shock are observed, one should only use formulas like Four Sovereigns, Six Sovereigns, or Yi Gong Powder, adding White Aconite to stabilize the wind, and Chaihu to soothe the liver, thus addressing issues at the root to prevent diarrhea and convulsions ensuring restoration of calm. If symptoms of vomiting, diarrhea, and convulsions have already been seen, yet one is still unaware of the necessity to reinforce the spleen and soothe the liver as a means of life preservation—using formulas like Bao Long or Zhen Jing—such knowledge indeed remains quite distant.[55p]

　　　　　暴泻

　　巢氏云：小儿卒利者，由肠胃虚，暴为冷热之气所伤而为卒利。热则色黄赤，冷则色青白，若冷热相交则变为赤白滞利也。
　　　　　久泻

　　大法补虚消积。
　　《凤髓经》歌云：脾中有积热迟留，致使终年泻不休。项软见人多哽气，更兼清水鼻中流。少间有似黄金色，若有垂肠更不收。形证又看胸膈上，胸前深赤汗如油。唇赤生疮眼脉赤，若不调脾命即休。
　　　　　飧泻

　　医书谓之水谷泻。食不消，脾胃冷，故不能消化，当补脾，益黄散主之。　　乳食不消，初病忽然气出冷，四肢亦冷。面白无光泽，精神不定，此乃胃气不和，可以大温药治之，使君子丸、益黄散主之。　　若病泄泻，日久不瘥，乳食不化，是脾胃有风冷，先服益黄散二服，后用宣风散导之。胃宜再补，宜参大科飧泄门用之。[56p]

Sudden Diarrhea

The Cai family states: When a child has sudden diarrhea, it is due to the weakness of the intestines and stomach, harmed by the sudden invasion of hot and cold air. If it is heat, the color will be yellow or red; if it is cold, the color will be blue or white. When hot and cold intersect, it will transform into a stasis of red and white diarrhea.

Chronic Diarrhea

The major treatment is to tonify the deficiency and resolve accumulation. The "Classics of Phoenix Essence" sings: In the spleen, there is stagnant heat causing persistent diarrhea throughout the year. The neck is soft and many people experience choking sensation, along with clear fluid flowing from the nose. At times, there is a golden-yellow appearance; if there is also prolapsed intestine, it will not retract. For physical manifestations, observe the chest and diaphragm; the chest is deeply red with sweat resembling oil. The lips are red, sores appear, and the eyes have a red pulse; if the spleen is not regulated, it may lead to death.

Food-related Diarrhea

Medical texts refer to this as dietary diarrhea. Food does not digest, and the spleen and stomach are cold, hence they cannot assimilate properly. It is necessary to tonify the spleen, using "Yihuang San" as the main treatment. If there is undigested milk food, the initial illness arises suddenly with cold air released, and the limbs are also cold. The face is pale and lacks luster, with unstable spirit; this indicates disharmony of stomach qi, which can be treated with warming medicines like "Junzi Pill" and "Yihuang San" as the main treatment. If the illness persists over a long time without recovery and milk food does not digest, there is wind-cold in the spleen and stomach. First take "Yihuang San" twice, then follow with "Xuanfeng San" to guide it out. The stomach needs further tonification, and it is advisable to refer to major prescriptions for dietary diarrhea.[56p]

　　　　小儿卫生总微论方 【宋　撰人未详】
　　　　　吐泻

　　小儿吐泻者，皆由脾胃虚弱，乳哺不调，风寒暑湿，邪干于正之所致也。其证不一，今条叙之：　　吐啘哯
　　吐逆，自生下便吐者，此是儿初生之时，拭掠口中秽血不尽，因咽入喉故也。　　吐逆，胸膈满闷气急者，此因儿啼哭未定，气息未匀，乳母忽遽以乳饲之，儿气尚逆，乳不得下，停滞于胸膈之间，因更饮乳，前后相沓，气不宣通，故气逆而乳随出之为吐也。宜调其气而止吐。古书亦曰：大哭之后，食乳者多成吐泻也。　　吐逆，腹胀喘息，乳不化，夹青水，面青唇白者，此周乳母胃寒取凉，食冷饮寒，致冷气入乳，变坏其汁，而不捻去，仍以饲儿；或能食者，因以冷物饲之，其冷乳冷食入腹，与气相搏，伤于脾胃，则气逆而此也。其证若此，宜温胃止吐调气。[57p]

Discussion on Pediatric Hygiene: Vomiting and Diarrhea

The vomiting and diarrhea in children stem from a weakness of the spleen and stomach, irregularities in breastfeeding, and external influences such as wind, cold, heat, and dampness interfering with the body's proper functions. The symptoms vary, and are described as follows:

  1. Vomiting from birth: If a child vomits immediately after birth, it is due to residual foul blood in the mouth being swallowed into the throat.

  2. Vomiting and retching, with fullness in the chest and rapid breathing: This occurs when the infant cries excessively and breathes irregularly, and the mother abruptly feeds them milk. When the child still has reversed airflow, it prevents the milk from going down, causing it to stagnate in the chest, leading to vomiting as the milk follows the reversed air. It is advisable to regulate the airflow to stop the vomiting. Ancient texts also mention that crying excessively before feeding often leads to vomiting and diarrhea.

  3. Vomiting with abdominal distension, wheezing, undigested milk, mixed with greenish water, and a pale complexion: This is caused by the breastfeeding mother's stomach being cold and consuming cold food and drinks, which introduces cold energy into the milk, spoiling its quality and not being eliminated before feeding the child. Alternatively, if the mother feeds the child with cold items, the cold milk and food will clash with the air in the stomach, harming the spleen and stomach, leading to reversed airflow. In such cases, it is advisable to warm the stomach to stop the vomiting and regulate the airflow.[57p]

若伤重有停滞者，以稳药磨化，不可快下，恐脾胃愈虚而生风也。凡风冷变坏之乳，当捻去之，暂断乳儿，令乳母服药温腹，然后饲儿。若不捻去，非只令儿吐逆，肠胃虚者，冷因得入，亦下利也。　　吐逆，身热，吐奶成片子者，胃有热也。此因乳冒热，或因饮酒，热入其乳，变坏其汁，而不捻出，仍以饲儿；或儿乘热哺啜，致热气入胃，与气相搏，致气逆而吐也。其证若此，如久有积热者，必四肢生疮，多渴而面黄，宜微下之。虚者，以稳药磨化，后调其气。　　吐逆，身热鼻青，呵欠烦闷，口中气热，夜间发躁者，此伤风吐也。因解脱失宜，风冷袭之，搏于血气，故身热呵欠，烦闷口中气热也。气不得顺，故逆而作吐也。[58p]

If there is significant injury with stagnation, one should use stabilizing medicine to alleviate it; do not rush to take action, for fear that the spleen and stomach may become more deficient and generate wind. For all milk that has turned bad due to wind and cold, it should be squeezed out, and the breastfeeding child should be temporarily weaned. The wet nurse should take medicine to warm her abdomen before feeding the child again. If the milk is not squeezed out, it not only causes the child to vomit but can also allow cold to enter the already deficient stomach and intestines, leading to diarrhea.

For vomiting, fever, and curdled milk, there is heat in the stomach. This may be due to the milk being overheated, or from consuming alcohol, which heats the milk, spoiling its quality, and if not squeezed out, it continues to be fed to the child. Alternatively, if the child nurses while hot, the heat can enter the stomach, battling with vital energy and causing a reverse reaction, leading to vomiting. If the symptoms are like this, and there has been a buildup of heat for a long time, sores will likely develop on the limbs, accompanied by excessive thirst and a yellowish complexion; gentle purgation is advisable. In the case of deficiency, use stabilizing medicine to alleviate it, then regulate the vital energy.

For vomiting, fever, cyanotic nose, yawning, restlessness, and hot breath at night, this is due to a cold invasion causing vomiting. This occurs due to improper release, where cold wind attacks the blood and energy, hence the fever, yawning, and restlessness with hot breath. If the energy cannot flow smoothly, this results in a reverse reaction and vomiting.[58p]

宜调气止吐，发散风冷。　　吐逆，唇黑面黄，多啼有痰，吐气臭者，此脾胃有伤也，宜先下之，后调其气。　　吐逆，早晚发热，睡卧不安者，此惊吐也。心热则生惊，故睡卧不安而神不宁也。心神不宁，则气血逆乱而吐也。宜与镇惊去热止吐。　　吐逆，面晄白无精光，口中气冷，口频撮，不思乳食，吐水者，胃气不和也，宜补脾胃。　　吐逆，痰涎色黄，稠粘上壅者，胃热也。若吐痰涎白渌或吐沫者，胃虚冷也。热者宜微利之，冷者宜温补之。　　吐逆痰涎及有血者，此肺热也。久则肺虚成痿。[59p]

It is advisable to regulate the qi to stop vomiting and disperse wind and cold.

For vomit and nausea, with black lips and a yellow face, frequent crying with phlegm, and foul breath, this indicates damage to the spleen and stomach; it is wise to first purge, then regulate the qi.

For vomit and nausea that occur with fever in the morning and evening, and disturbed sleep, this indicates shock-induced vomiting. Heart heat leads to shock, which disrupts sleep and causes restlessness. When the heart is unsettled, qi and blood become chaotic, resulting in vomiting. Therefore, it is necessary to calm the shock, eliminate heat, and stop the vomiting.

For vomit and nausea with a pale face lacking vitality, cold breath in the mouth, frequent swallowing without desire for food, and vomiting water, this suggests disharmony in the stomach qi; it is advisable to tonify the spleen and stomach.

For vomit and nausea with yellow phlegm that is thick and obstructive, this signifies stomach heat. If the expelled phlegm is white and thin or foamy, the stomach is in a state of deficiency and cold. The hot condition should be treated with slight purging, while the cold condition should be supplemented with warmth.

For vomit, nausea, and the presence of blood, this indicates lung heat. If protracted, it can lead to lung deficiency and atrophy.[59p]

昔钱乙治段斋郎子四岁，身热吐痰，嗽数日而咯血，他医以桔梗汤、防己圆治之不愈，涎上攻吐喘不止。遂请乙治。乙下褊银圆一大服，复以补肺汤、补脾散为治。乙曰：此子咯血，肺虚也。肺虽咯血，有热故也。久则虚痿。今涎上潮而吐，当下其涎。若不吐涎，则不甚便，盖吐涎能虚又生惊也。痰实上攻，亦能发搐。依法只宜先下痰而后补脾肺，必涎上而吐愈为顺治也，若先补肺为逆耳。乙所用药方，本集载之，此所谓识病之轻重先后为治也。　　啘哯者，比吐逆异也。吐者，乃邪搏胃气，逆而上行，谷不能传化，随气出也。啘者，但气逆而欲吐，吐则谷无所出，故俗谓干呕也。哯者，乃儿因吮乳汁过多，胃满而上溢出也，故俗呼谓之噫奶，当便与空乳令吮即定。若频久吮之，亦能为病。[60p]

In the past, when Qian Yi treated the four-year-old son of Duan Zhai, the boy had a fever, was coughing up phlegm, and had coughed up blood for several days. Other doctors used Platycodon Decoction and Stephania Powder but had no success. The boy continued to cough, with phlegm rising, and could not stop wheezing. Thus, they requested Yi to treat him. He prescribed a large dose of an emetic and also used Lung Nourishing Decoction and Spleen Strengthening Powder as treatment. Yi stated: This child is coughing up blood due to lung deficiency. Although he coughs up blood, it is because of heat. Over time, it can lead to weakness. Currently, the phlegm is rising, and he is vomiting; we need to expel that phlegm. If he does not vomit the phlegm, it will not be very beneficial, as expelling the phlegm can weaken him and also cause panic. When the phlegm is obstructing upward, it can also lead to convulsions. Therefore, it is appropriate to first resolve the phlegm and then nourish the spleen and lungs; it is vital to expel the phlegm for a proper treatment. If we first nourish the lungs, it would be contrary to the approach. The medicinal formula used by Yi is recorded in the collection; this is what is meant by understanding the priorities in treating diseases.

The terms "retching" and "vomiting" differ. Vomiting occurs when evil forces obstruct the stomach Qi, causing it to reverse and rise, preventing the transformation and movement of food, thus being expelled with the Qi. Retching, on the other hand, is merely the Qi reversing and the desire to vomit, but if vomiting occurs, food will not be expelled, hence it is commonly referred to as dry heaving. Retching can also happen when a child sucks too much milk, causing the stomach to overflow, which is commonly termed "milk overflow." To remedy this, it is best to let the child suck an empty breast immediately. However, if they continue to suck frequently for a long time, it can also lead to illness.[60p]

　　　　　泻

　　泻色白者，冷泻也。此由小儿肠胃虚弱，因解脱，风冷干之；或因会寒饮冷，入于肠胃，冷气相搏为利下也。其色白，面白或腹痛者，并宜调中。若又伤风冷，前后重沓，冷甚则泻不止而为泄注也。　　泻色赤者，热泻也。此由小儿肠胃本挟虚热，而风冷乘之，入于肠胃之间，热气相搏而为利下，故其色赤也。宜微下之以导其热，后调其气。　　泻色乍赤乍白，或水或谷者，此冷热泻也，由小儿肠胃，先因有冷而复伤热，或先因有热而复伤冷，肠胃宿虚，冷热交攻而为利下，宜调其冷热，和养其气。　　泻色黄赤红黑者，皆热也。赤黑者有毒，并微下之，然后调气。　　泻色青发热，有时睡卧不安者，此惊泻也。小儿粪黄，脾胃土之本色也。[61p]

Diarrhea

Diarrhea that is white in color is considered cold diarrhea. This occurs when a child's stomach and intestines are weak, leading to an expulsion of wind and cold, or due to consuming cold foods and drinks that enter the stomach and intestines, causing coldness to clash and result in diarrhea. If the stool is white and accompanied by a pale face or abdominal pain, one should harmonize the middle. If there is also an injury from wind and cold, with repeated bouts, and if the cold is severe, then diarrhea may become persistent and lead to a more serious condition.

Diarrhea that is red in color is considered hot diarrhea. This happens when a child’s stomach and intestines are originally accompanied by excessive heat, and wind and cold invade, conflicting and leading to diarrhea, which is why it appears red. In this case, it is advisable to mildly purge to guide out the heat and then regulate the qi.

Diarrhea that alternates between red and white, or is watery or contains grains, is known as mixed cold and hot diarrhea. This occurs when a child’s stomach and intestines have first experienced cold and then suffered from heat, or vice versa. With underlying weakness, the alternating effects of cold and heat cause diarrhea, thus one should adjust the balance of hot and cold and nourish the qi.

Diarrhea with colors of yellow, red, or black, all indicate heat. Red and black indicate toxicity, so one should mildly purge and then regulate the qi.

Diarrhea appearing green and accompanied by fever, or sometimes unrest during sleep, indicates shock-induced diarrhea. A child's stool is yellow, which is the natural color related to the spleen and stomach.[61p]

色青，肝木为风，肝木来刑脾土，宜早治之，不尔，则变脾风而发瘈瘲，则难治也。所谓粪青者，须才便下，便色青是也。若初下时黄，良久乃青者非也。小儿安者皆然，不可认为青粪也。若泻色青白，谷不化者，此谓冷也。宜温补脾胃，发散风冷。　　泻灙下色赤白，腹大上青筋见，发稀饶啼，或吃泥土，时有蛔虫，此疳泻也，宜止泻退疳。　　泻多日，唇口及粪色皆白，粪颇多者，久因成冷，脾胃衰困，恐变脾风发癎，宜防备，温养补助脾胃。　　泻于暑热时多患者，谓时热及饮食皆冷故也。不伤于热，必伤于冷。若伤热伏暑而泻者。则心脏烦热，必小便不利，清浊不分。泻色赤黄，宜利小便，解暑热。若小便快而泻者，冷泻也，色必青白，谷不化，宜温脾胃止泻。　　泻者，不可急以热药止之，多变为痢而下脓血也。当审察冷热证候，详度缓急施治也。[62p]

The color is green; the liver associated with wood represents wind. The liver's wood influences the spleen's earth, so it should be treated early. Otherwise, it may transform into spleen wind and provoke epilepsy, making it difficult to cure. The so-called green stool must be a quick and immediate response; the stool appearing blue is thus. If initially yellow and then later blue, it is not considered so. Children generally appear so; it should not be regarded as green stool. If diarrhea is a bluish white color, and food is not digested, it is called cold. Warmly tonify the spleen and stomach to dispel wind and cold.

If diarrhea is reddish and white, with a distended abdomen and visible blue veins, producing watery stools accompanied by crying, or if consuming soil and worms present intermittently, this indicates malabsorption diarrhea. It should be treated to stop the diarrhea and resolve malabsorption.

If diarrhea lasts several days, and the lips, mouth, and stool are all white, and there is considerable stool, this indicates chronic cold, with weakened spleen and stomach, risking a transformation to spleen wind causing epilepsy. Preventive measures should be taken to warm and nourish the spleen and stomach.

Diarrhea occurring during a hot season is often due to heat and cold food. It is not harmed by heat but rather by cold. If heat injures and causes diarrhea, then there will be irritability and heat in the heart, and urination will be obstructed, with the distinction between clear and turbid lost. Diarrhea of a red-yellow color suggests promoting urination to alleviate summer heat. If urination occurs frequently with diarrhea, it indicates cold diarrhea, which is typically bluish white, with undigested food. It is advisable to warm the spleen and stomach to stop the diarrhea.

For diarrhea, one should not hasten to use hot remedies to stop it, as this often transforms into dysentery with pus and blood. The conditions of hot and cold should be carefully examined, and treatment should be adjusted according to the severity and urgency.[62p]

　　　　　吐泻

　　吐泻多病于春夏秋三时，惟冬时绝少者，盖吐泻皆因脾胃虚冷热所致，以冬时阳气在内，多食温暖，少饮水浆故也。设有患者，必因伤于乳食也。若春时病吐泻者多因于风，夏时病者多因于热，秋时病者多因于冷。凡治吐泻者，必当审其时候，观其形证，察其温凉寒热，如此则无误矣。[63p]

Vomiting and Diarrhea

Vomiting and diarrhea are most common in the spring, summer, and autumn, while rarely occurring in winter. This is because both conditions arise from a deficiency of the spleen and stomach, affected by cold and heat. In winter, yang energy is predominant, with an abundance of warm food and limited intake of liquids. If a patient is afflicted, it is usually due to damage from dairy and other foods. When vomiting and diarrhea occur in spring, they are often caused by wind; in summer, by heat; and in autumn, by cold. In treating vomiting and diarrhea, one must carefully consider the season, observe the symptoms, and assess the conditions of warmth, coolness, cold, and heat. Only then can one avoid mistakes.[63p]

　　　　　伤风吐泻

　　伤风吐泻、身温，乍凉乍热，呵欠烦闷，多睡，口中气粗，如先已曾经下或无下证。慎不可下也。此由脾肺受寒，不能入脾也。更有五脏兼见之证。发散者，大青膏服之；补脾者，后服益黄散。此钱乙所用药也。　　伤风吐泻，身热多睡，能乳，呵欠烦闷，口中气热，饮水不止，吐痰，大便黄水，此为胃虚热渴吐泻也，当生胃中津液以止其渴。钱乙用白朮煎汤服之，然后发散风冷，亦用大青膏。又云：吐泻昏睡露睛者，胃虚热也。吐泻昏睡不露睛者，胃实热也。　　伤风吐泻，身凉吐沫，泻青白色，呵欠闷乱不渴，哽气，长出气，睡露睛，此伤风荏苒轻怯，因成吐泻，当先补脾。钱乙先用益黄散，后发散其风，用大青膏。此二病于春冬多也。[64p]

Wind Cold and Diarrhea

When affected by wind cold and experiencing vomiting and diarrhea, the body temperature fluctuates between hot and cold, accompanied by yawning, restlessness, excessive sleep, coarse breathing, and possible previous purging or absence of symptoms. It is crucial not to purge again. This condition arises from the spleen and lungs being chilled, hindering their function. There may be symptoms affecting the five internal organs. For those with a dispersing nature, use Da Qing Paste; for those who need to tonify the spleen, follow with Yi Huang Powder. These are the medications used by Qian Yi.

When experiencing wind cold, vomiting, diarrhea, with fever and excessive sleep, the ability to nurse, yawning, restlessness, hot breath, continuous thirst, phlegm vomiting, and yellow water in the stools, this indicates stomach heat and thirst from deficiency. One should generate body fluids to quench thirst. Qian Yi suggests taking a decoction of Bai Zhu and then dispersing the wind cold, also using Da Qing Paste. Additionally, if a person has symptoms of vomiting and diarrhea with drowsiness and visibly opened eyes, this indicates stomach heat; if they are drowsy without visible eye exposure, it indicates excess stomach heat.

In cases of wind cold, with coolness, frothy saliva, diarrhea that is light blue or white, yawning, restlessness without thirst, difficult breathing, prolonged exhalation, and drowsiness with opened eyes, this is a light and timid presentation of wind cold leading to vomiting and diarrhea, where one should first tonify the spleen. Qian Yi first recommends Yi Huang Powder, followed by dispersing the wind with Da Qing Paste. These two illnesses occur more frequently in spring and winter.[64p]

　　　　　伤食吐乳

　　吐泻乳食不化，其吐及粪皆有酸臭气者，此伤食吐泻也。凡吐乳泻黄赤者，伤热乳食也；若吐乳泻青白者，伤冷乳食也。并宜微下之，后和胃。气虚者，以缓化滞药渐磨化之。　　吐泻在初生三日内，壮热不乳，大便乳不消化或白色者，是伤乳，当微与下，后和胃。气虚者，以缓化滞药渐磨化之。　　吐泻在初生三日已上至十日，身温凉，不思乳，大便青白，乳不消化，此上实下虚也，更有五脏兼见证，泻其所实者而补其脾胃虚者也。　　吐泻有兼脏证者，兼肺则睡露睛喘气，兼心则惊悸饮水，兼脾则困倦饶睡 【吐泻乃脾胃之本病，】兼肝则呵欠烦闷，兼肾则不语畏明。[65p]

Injury from Food Leading to Vomiting and Diarrhea

Vomiting and diarrhea with undigested milk and food, accompanied by a sour and foul odor, indicate an injury from food. If the vomit and stools are yellow or red, this is due to excessive heat from milk and food; if the vomit and stools are green or white, it results from cold milk and food. In both cases, a gentle purgative is advisable, followed by harmonizing the stomach. For those with deficient qi, use mild remedies to gradually alleviate the stagnation.

If vomiting and diarrhea occur within the first three days of birth, accompanied by strong heat and lack of appetite for milk, or with undigested white stools, this signifies a milk injury. A mild purgative should be administered, followed by harmonizing the stomach. For those with deficient qi, use mild remedies to gradually alleviate the stagnation.

If vomiting and diarrhea persist from three days up to ten days after birth, with body heat that feels cool, lack of desire for milk, blue or white stools, and undigested milk, this indicates a condition of excess above and deficiency below. There may also be evidence of involvement of the five organs, thus purging the excess while supplementing the deficient spleen and stomach.

In cases where vomiting and diarrhea are accompanied by organ symptoms, involvement of the lungs may show as drowsiness and wheezing; involvement of the heart may cause palpitations upon drinking; involvement of the spleen may lead to fatigue and excessive sleep. If the liver is affected, signs may include yawning and irritability; if the kidneys are involved, there may be muteness and a fear of light.[65p]

　　　　　冷热吐泻

　　吐泻在五月中已后身壮热者，此热也，小儿脏腑中十分中九分热。此因伤热乳，或胃热入内，吐乳不消，泻深赤色，宜与解热，钱乙用玉露散。　　吐泻在六月中已后，身大温而似热，脏腑中六分热四分冷也。呕吐乳食不消，泻色黄多白少似褐，或食乳或不食乳，宜少补脾而大解热，钱乙少用益黄散，多用玉露散。更宜审察冷热，如儿大热泻色赤黄者，此热多，依五月中后治之。　　吐泻在七月中已后，身温，脏腑中三分热七分冷也。[66p]

Cold and Hot Vomiting and Diarrhea

Vomiting and diarrhea occurring after mid-May with a strong fever is associated with heat in the body. In this case, the internal organs of a child have nine parts heat and one part cold. This is due to overconsumption of hot milk or heat entering the stomach, causing the milk to not digest, resulting in deep red diarrhea. It is advisable to use medication to clear the heat, as suggested by Qian Yi, who recommended the use of Yu Lu San.

Vomiting and diarrhea occurring after mid-June with significant warmth that resembles heat indicates that there is six parts heat and four parts cold in the internal organs. There may be vomiting of undigested milk or food, and the diarrhea appears yellow with more white and a semblance of brown; this might occur regardless of whether milk is ingested or not. It is advisable to slightly nourish the spleen and emphasize clearing heat, as Qian Yi suggested using a lesser amount of Yi Huang San and more of Yu Lu San. Additionally, careful observation of the balance of heat and cold is necessary. If a child has intense heat with red or yellow diarrhea, this indicates excessive heat, and treatment should follow the protocols of after mid-May.

Vomiting and diarrhea occurring after mid-July manifest as warmth, with three parts heat and seven parts cold in the internal organs.[66p]

不能食乳，多似睡，闷乱，哽气，长出气，睡露睛，唇白，多啘而不渴，钱乙于食前令多服补脾益黄散，于食后少服解热玉露散。更宜相度冷热，若身大温，泻后黄者，依六月中已后为治也。　　吐泻在八月中已后，身冷无阳也。不能食乳，干啘，泻青褐水，钱乙只用益黄散补脾，不可下。　　吐泻所论冷热时月，此以中原之地言，今较之江浙则气候不伺。今江浙之地二三月尚寒，四五月温暖，六月入伏之后才热，七月热盛，八月热尚未退，虽冬月晴多便暖，虽夏月阴多便寒，不可概以中原冷热时候便为定论。经所谓东西南北之异地，温凉寒热之异宜。况每岁寒热，自随时令早晚，难以拘定月日也。候之者，乘其至也，谓至其热则从热治，至其温则从温治，至其寒则从寒治。[67p]

One should not consume milk, as it resembles sleep; it causes stuffiness, turmoil, and a feeling of blocked energy, along with prolonged breath, sleepiness with opened eyes, pale lips, and a tendency to sip frequently without thirst. Qian Yi suggests taking a lot of Supplementing the Spleen and Nourishing the Yellow Powder before meals, and only a little of the Cooling Jade Dew Powder after meals. It is essential to observe the changes in temperature; if the body feels too warm and there is yellow diarrhea after purging, one should treat it based on what's customary after mid-June.

For vomiting and diarrhea that occur after mid-August, if the body feels cold and lacks yang, one should not consume milk, and if there is dry cough and greenish-brown watery diarrhea, Qian Yi advises using only the Nourishing Yellow Powder to supplement the spleen and not to purge.

The discussions of heat and cold based on time and month pertain to the Central Plains; however, compared to Jiangzhou and Zhejiang, the climate is different. The regions of Jiangzhou and Zhejiang remain chilly in February and March, warm in April and May, and only heat up after entering the summer solstice in June. July is hot, and August's heat has not yet receded. Even during winter, many sunny days feel warm, while many cloudy summer days feel cold; thus, one cannot strictly apply the seasonal temperatures of the Central Plains as a universal conclusion.

The texts mention differences based on geography, with variations in warmth and coolness. Furthermore, each year's heat and cold follow the seasons' cycles, making it difficult to strictly define specific days or months. One should observe the conditions as they arise: treat heat with heat, warmth with warmth, and cold with cold.[67p]

至其凉则从凉治，此乃随四时之气，各适其宜。　　吐泻于夏秋大热之时，伏暑伤冷则心脏烦躁，小便不利，清浊不分，阴阳二气相干，名曰气乱。乱于肠胃之间，名曰霍乱。其证乘热伤冷，气逆而喘，腹胁胀满，身热脉乱，头痛体疼，如伤寒之状，上即大吐，下即大泻；重者四肢厥冷，脚胫转筋。法当调顺其气，分别清浊，升降阴阳。若只伏暑吐泻者，则小便不利，其证虽与上证稍同而轻，非霍乱比，泻色赤黄，此但只名伏暑吐泻，不为霍乱也。[68p]

When it becomes cool, treat it with coolness; this aligns with the seasonal changes, each suitable for its time. Diarrhea and vomiting during the heat of summer and autumn, where summer heat harms cold, lead to agitation of the heart, difficulty in urination, confusion between clear and turbid, and the disruption of yin and yang, are referred to as "qi disturbance." Disturbance between the stomach and intestines is termed "cholera." Symptoms arise from heat injuring cold, causing qi to reverse, resulting in cough, abdominal and flank fullness, elevated body temperature, disordered pulse, headaches, and body aches, resembling the signs of a cold; the upper part manifests as severe vomiting, the lower as severe diarrhea; in severe cases, the limbs may become cold and cramps occur in the legs. The method should regulate the qi, distinguish between clear and turbid, and manage the rise and fall of yin and yang. If symptoms are solely due to summer heat causing vomiting and diarrhea, there will be difficulty in urination, though the symptoms may resemble the previous ones but are milder and not comparable to cholera. The diarrhea will appear reddish-yellow; this condition is simply termed "summer heat vomiting and diarrhea," not cholera.[68p]

　　治霍乱吐泻，若热多而渴者五苓散；寒多不渴，而心腹身体疼痛，及烦躁渴不能饮者，可服理中汤；寒甚腹痛转筋，四肢拘急者，理中汤加附子；汗出恶寒，手足厥冷，下利清谷，内寒外热，脉微欲绝者，并四逆汤。已上诸证病，可与香薷散服之，以他药不能疗此证也。治伏暑吐泻，若小便不利，与五苓散利小便，及与香薷散解伏暑，坯莲散、救生丹止吐。　　吐泻不拘何时，则令脾胃虚弱，多致生风而为脾风慢惊也。以脾土衰而肝木来刑故　。当补脾胃，不令困弱，则风不生而病易愈也。　　吐泻已定未定，烦渴者，皆津液内耗也，不问新久，宜煎钱乙白朮散，使满意取足饮之，多即愈好，不尔即津液内耗而引饮不止，内生其热，外邪相干，则证变百端以成他病，渐至危困也。
　　　　幼幼近编 【明　陈治】
[69p]

To treat cholera characterized by vomiting and diarrhea, if there is excessive heat and thirst, use Wuling Powder; if there is excessive cold without thirst, accompanied by pain in the heart and abdomen and restlessness with an inability to drink, one may take Lizhong Decoction; if there is severe cold with abdominal pain and cramping, and the limbs are tense, add Aconite to Lizhong Decoction; if sweating occurs with a feeling of cold, with cold hands and feet, diarrhea with clear stools, internal cold and external heat, and the pulse is feeble and about to cease, use Sini Decoction. For the aforementioned diseases, one may take Xiangru Powder, as other medicines cannot treat these conditions.

To treat heatstroke-induced vomiting and diarrhea, if there is difficulty in urination, administer Wuling Powder to facilitate urination, and use Xiangru Powder to alleviate heatstroke. For persistent vomiting, use Pill of the Lotus Seed or Rescuer Elixir to stop it.

Regardless of the timing of vomiting and diarrhea, it indicates weakness of the spleen and stomach, often leading to wind arising as "spleen wind" causing prolonged distress. This results from the spleen being weakened and the liver imposing its influence. Therefore, it is important to nourish the spleen and stomach to prevent them from being overwhelmed, so that wind does not arise and recovery becomes easier.

If vomiting and diarrhea have not completely resolved and there is thirst, it indicates internal consumption of fluids. Regardless of whether the condition is new or old, one should prepare and drink Qianyi Baizhu Powder to ensure adequate fluid intake. The more one drinks, the more favorable the outcome. Otherwise, internal fluid consumption will result in persistent thirst and the generation of heat, with external pathogens complicating the condition, leading to various symptoms and potentially severe complications.[69p]

　　　　　吐泻

　　小儿吐泻，有热、有寒、有虚、有积、有惊，但因乳母所伤而致者为多。凡手指热则胃热，手指冷则胃寒；腹痛欲按者属虚，不可按者属实。寒者气暖神清，面白肢冷，吐乳不消，粪色青白，宜理中汤或异功散加藿香、肉果、砂仁。热者食乳即吐，四肢五心烦热，唇红作渴，粪沫焦黄，小便赤少，泻黄散加木通、滑石。伤暑者，藿香饮或五苓散。伤乳食者，昏睡嗳气，不思乳食，肚热脚冷，吐出酸秽，泻如败卵，腹不可按，宜保和丸或平胃散加曲芽、半夏、丁香。伤风者，身温乍热乍寒，咳嗽气急，天麻散加防风。虚昔睡则露睛，吐乳不消，泻粪不变，懒贪乳食，手指常冷，腹痛喜按，异功散、白朮散、助胃膏。惊者，面色青黄，乳食不化，泄泻青色，宜六君子汤加柴胡、钓藤、木香。大抵先吐后泻者，多属于热；先泻后吐者，多属于虚。有但吐不泻，但泻不吐者，宜于大方脉中参治，又当根其致病之由而药之，不可拘于吐泻上着力也。[70p]

Vomiting and Diarrhea

In cases of children experiencing vomiting and diarrhea, there may be heat, cold, deficiency, accumulation, or fright; however, many cases arise from harm done by the wet nurse. Generally, if the fingertips are warm, it indicates heat in the stomach; if cold, it indicates cold in the stomach. If there is abdominal pain that the child wants to press, it belongs to deficiency; if it cannot be pressed, it belongs to excess.

In cold cases, the child’s energy is warm, the spirit clear, the face pale, and the limbs cold; there is vomiting without digestion, and the stool is blue-white. This requires the use of "Li Zhong Tang" or "Yi Gong San" with the addition of mint, peach kernel, and cardamom.

In heat cases, upon consuming milk, the child vomits; the limbs and palms are agitated and hot, the lips are red and thirsty, the stool is yellowish-brown, and there is scant, red urine. For this, add wood lotus and talc to "Xie Huang San."

For cases of heatstroke, "Huo Xiang Yin" or "Wu Ling San" is appropriate. For those harmed by milk or food, there is drowsiness with belching, a lack of interest in milk or food, a hot belly, and cold feet; the vomit is sour and foul, the diarrhea resembles rotting eggs, and the abdomen cannot be pressed. Treatment should be with "Bao He Wan" or "Ping Wei San" with the addition of malt, Pinellia ternata, and clove.

For cases of wind harm, the child alternates between warmth and cold, coughs with shortness of breath; use "Tian Ma San" with the addition of angelica and lignum sappan.

In deficiency cases, if they sleep with open eyes, vomit without digestion, have unchanged stools, are lethargic and crave milk, with cold hands and fingers, pain in the abdomen that they like to press; employ "Yi Gong San," "Bai Zhu San," and "Support the Stomach Paste."

For fright cases, the complexion is blue-yellow, food does not digest, diarrhea is blue-green; "Liu Jun Zi Tang" with the addition of bupleurum, smartweed, and aromatic wood is indicated.

In general, if vomiting occurs before diarrhea, it mostly relates to heat; if diarrhea occurs before vomiting, it typically indicates deficiency. If there is only vomiting without diarrhea, or only diarrhea without vomiting, one should treat from the pulse in the major diagnosis while also addressing the root cause of the illness with medicine, and not just focus on the symptoms of vomiting and diarrhea.[70p]

Formulas[71p]

　　白朮圆 【《中藏经》】 　治小儿白泻。　　白朮　当归　芍药　木香减半
　　右等分为末，炼蜜圆如菉豆大，每服十圆十五圆，不拘时候，米饮下。
　　藿香汤 【《千金方》】 　治毒气吐下，腹胀逆，害乳哺。　　藿香一两　生姜二两　青竹茹　甘草各半两　　右四味(口父)咀，以水二升，煮取八合，每服一合，日三。有热加升麻半两。
　　五味异功散 【《小儿直诀》，下同】 　治脾胃虚弱。　　人参　茯苓　白朮　甘草炒　陈皮各等分　　右为末，每服三钱，盖枣水煎。一方加木香。薛己曰：按前方补脾胃之圣药也。况人之一身，以脾胃为主，若小儿乳食失节，寒凉失宜，或乳母六淫七情失调，儿饮其乳，诸病顿起，当专以此药治之，其应如向。王肯堂曰：愚按前方治脾胃虚弱，吐泻不食，或惊搐痰盛，或睡而露睛，手足指冷，或脾胃虚弱，咳嗽吐痰，或虚热上攻，口舌生疮，弄舌流涎。若母有证，致儿患此者，母并服之。[72p]

Bai Zhu Yuan: Treats children’s diarrhea. Bai Zhu, Dang Gui, Shao Yao, and Mu Xiang (half). Grind the above ingredients to a powder, and roll them into pills about the size of a mung bean. Take ten to fifteen pills each time, regardless of the time, with rice drink.

Huo Xiang Tang: Treats toxic gas causing vomiting, abdominal distention, and harming breastfeeding. One liang of Huo Xiang, two liang of fresh ginger, half a liang each of Qing Zhu Ru and Gan Cao. Chew the four ingredients, then boil with two sheng of water to obtain eight cups. Take one cup three times a day. If heat is present, add half a liang of Sheng Ma.

Wu Wei Yi Gong San: Treats weak spleen and stomach. Equal parts of Ren Shen, Fu Ling, Bai Zhu, and stir-fried Gan Cao, and Chen Pi. Grind to a powder, and take three qian, decocted in jujube water. One variation adds Mu Xiang. Xue Ji states that this is a sacred remedy for tonifying the spleen and stomach. The human body places great importance on the spleen and stomach. If children have irregular feeding and cold intake, or if the nursing mother is affected by emotional disturbances, causing various ailments in the child, this medicine should be specifically used to treat it, and it works effectively. Wang Kentang notes that this formula treats weak spleen and stomach, vomiting, diarrhea, poor appetite, or symptoms of fright, excessive phlegm, hand and foot coldness, or weak spleen and stomach with cough and phlegm, or upward heat causing sores in the mouth and tongue, drooling. If the mother exhibits symptoms that affect the child, she should also take it.[72p]

　　益黄散　治脾土虚寒，呕吐泻泄。
　　青皮下食，入太阴仓　丁香各二钱，去脾胃中寒　诃子肉五钱，能开胃消食止痢　甘草炙，三钱　陈皮二钱半　　右为末，每服一二钱，水煎。薛己曰：按前证若因脾土虚弱而吐泻者，用五味异功散。若因肝木侮脾土而吐泻者，用六君子加柴胡；如不应或手足指冷，属脾胃虚寒也，更加木香、炮姜。若因乳母脾土虚而肝木侮，亦治以前药。若乳母郁怒，致儿患前证，母服加味归脾汤。[73p]

Yihuang Powder is used to treat spleen and stomach deficiency with cold, leading to vomiting and diarrhea. The ingredients include:

  • Aconitum (Qingpi) – 2 qian (6 grams), to resolve food stagnation and enter the Taiyin;
  • Clove (Dingxiang) – 2 qian, to expel cold from the spleen and stomach;
  • Hezi fruit (Hezi) – 5 qian, to stimulate appetite, aid digestion, and stop diarrhea;
  • Honey-fried licorice (Gancao, zhi) – 3 qian;
  • Aged tangerine peel (Chenpi) – 2.5 qian.

The above should be ground into a powder. Each dose is 1-2 qian, to be decocted in water.

Xue Ji notes: If the nausea and diarrhea stem from the weakness of the spleen soil, use Wuwei Yigong Powder. If it arises from the liver's wood harming the spleen soil, use Six Gentlemen Decoction with Chai Hu added. If there is no response or if there are cold hands and feet, indicating cold in the spleen and stomach, then add Mu Xiang and roasted ginger. If a nursing mother has a weak spleen leading to liver wood harming her child, the same medicines can be used. If the mother is angry and this affects the child, she should take an enhanced version of Gui Pi Decoction.[73p]

　　人参安胃散　治因服峻剂，脾胃亏损，或成慢惊，泄泻呕吐，或肠胃有热以致前证。　　黄芪蜜炙，二钱　生甘草　炙甘草各五分　白芍七分　白茯四分　黄连二分　人参一钱　　右为末，每服二三钱，水煎。

　　七味白朮散　治吐泻或病后津液不足，口干作渴。　　干葛二钱，能鼓胃气上行，生津液，阳明经药也　人参　白朮炒　木香　白茯苓　甘草炙　藿香叶各一钱　　右为末，每服二三钱，水煎。《幼科全书》加乌梅，为治渴之圣药。发热渴者去木香。吐痛加芍药。薛己曰：按胃伤则呕，脾伤则泻，故用前药调补买气以化生津液。如无他证，只因胃气虚而津液不足者，用四君子汤尤效。[74p]

Ginseng Stomach Soothing Powder: It treats conditions due to the use of harsh medicines that have depleted the spleen and stomach, which may lead to chronic fright, diarrhea, and vomiting, or gastrointestinal heat causing the above symptoms. Ingredients: honey-fried Astragalus two qian, raw Licorice standard five fen, roasted Licorice five fen, white Peony seven fen, white Poria four fen, Coptis two fen, Ginseng one qian. Grind these into a powder. Take two to three qian each time, decoct in water.

Seven Flavor Atractylodes Powder: It treats vomiting and diarrhea or insufficient bodily fluids after illness, causing dry mouth and thirst. Ingredients: two qian of dried Kudzu, which can promote stomach qi to rise and generate fluids, is a Yangming channel medicine; Ginseng, fried Atractylodes, Mu Xiang, white Poria, roasted Licorice, and fragrant patchouli leaves each one qian. Grind these into a powder. Take two to three qian each time, decoct in water. In the "Complete Book on Pediatric Science," adding black plum is said to be a holy medicine for treating thirst. For those with fever and thirst, omit Mu Xiang. For vomiting pain, add Peony. Xue Ji states: In cases of stomach injury, there is vomiting; with spleen injury, there is diarrhea. Thus, the previous medicine is employed to adjust and replenish qi to generate fluids. If there are no other symptoms but simply spleen qi deficiency causing insufficient fluids, using the Four Gentlemen Decoction is especially effective.[74p]

　　四君子汤　治脾气虚弱，饮食不化，肠鸣泄泻，或呕哕吐逆。　　人参　白茯苓　白朮　甘草炙，各五分　　右，水煎服。

　　四物汤　治肝经血虚发热，日晡益甚，或烦躁不寐。　　当归　熟地黄各二钱　白芍药一钱　川芎五分　　右作二剂，水煎服。

　　八珍汤　治气血俱虚，或因失血过多，或因克伐元气，以致内热发热，肢体瘦瘁。　　即四物、四君二汤合服。

　　十全大补汤　治气血虚热，或因病后恶寒发热，或自汗盗汗，食少体倦，或发热作渴，头痛眩晕等证。即八珍汤加黄芪、肉桂。
　　六君子汤　治脾胃虚弱，体瘦面黄，或久患疟痢，不思乳食，或呕吐泄泻，饮食不化，或时患饮食停滞，或母有前证，致儿为患。　　人参　白朮　茯苓各二钱　陈皮　半夏　甘草炙，各一钱　　右每服二三钱，姜枣水煎。[75p]

Si Jun Zi Decoction: Treats deficiency of spleen qi, poor digestion, bowel sounds, diarrhea, or nausea and vomiting. Ingredients: Ginseng, white poria, white atractylodes, and licorice (each five grams). Prepare by boiling in water.

Si Wu Decoction: Treats heat due to deficiency of liver blood, worsens in the afternoon, or causes irritability and insomnia. Ingredients: Angelica sinensis, cooked rehmannia (each six grams), white peony (three grams), and chuanxiong (two grams). Make two doses, prepared by boiling in water.

Ba Zhen Decoction: Treats both qi and blood deficiency, whether due to excessive blood loss or depletion of vital energy, leading to internal heat and emaciation. This is a combination of Si Wu and Si Jun Zi decoctions.

Shi Quan Da Bu Decoction: Treats heat due to qi and blood deficiency, whether following an illness with chills and fever, or symptoms of spontaneous sweating, night sweats, decreased appetite, fatigue, or heat and thirst, with headache and dizziness. This is Ba Zhen Decoction plus astragalus and cinnamon.

Liu Jun Zi Decoction: Treats weakness of the spleen and stomach, emaciation and pallor, or chronic issues like malaria and dysentery, lack of appetite, vomiting and diarrhea, poor digestion, or occasional food stagnation. Also, if maternal issues lead to problems in the child. Ingredients: Ginseng, white atractylodes, poria (each six grams), dried tangerine peel, pinellia, and licorice (each three grams). For each dose, take two or three grams, boiled with ginger and jujube water.[75p]

　　补中益气汤　治中气不足，困睡发热，或元气虚弱，感冒风寒，或乳母劳役发热，致儿为患。　　黄芪炙　人参　白朮炒　甘草炙　当归　陈皮各五分　升麻　柴胡各二分　　右，姜枣水煎。

　　香砂助胃膏　治胃寒吐泻，乳食不化。　　人参　白朮炒　白茯苓各五钱　甘草炙　丁香各一钱，去胃中寒　砂仁四十个，下气消食　山药一两　白豆蔻十四个，宽胃暖脾进食　肉豆蔻四个，煨，温中补脾下气运化，非比香附、陈皮之快泄也　　右为末，炼蜜丸芡实大，每服二三丸，米饮磨化。一方加木香三钱。
　　人参养胃汤　治外感风寒，内伤生冷，寒热如疟，或呕逆恶心，平胃散中用厚朴，佐以苍朮正为泄上焦之湿，平胃土，不使太过而致其和耳，非温补脾胃也。　　人参　厚朴姜制　苍朮制，发汗　半夏汤泡　炙草二钱　草果仁虚弱不能者宜此　藿香　茯苓各五钱，调胃气　橘红二钱五分　　右每服二三钱，姜三片，乌梅一个，水煎。[76p]

Buzhong Yiqi Decoction treats insufficient middle qi, fatigue, fever, or weak vital energy due to wind-cold colds, or fever in nursing mothers from overwork, affecting their children. Ingredients: five parts each of roasted astragalus, ginseng, stir-fried white atractylodes, and roasted licorice; five parts each of angelica and dried tangerine peel; two parts each of elutherococcus and bupleurum. Boil with ginger and dates in water.

Xiangsha Zhiwei Paste treats stomach cold leading to vomiting and diarrhea, and indigestion from dairy and food. Ingredients: five qian each of ginseng, stir-fried white atractylodes, and white poria; one qian each of roasted licorice and clove to dispel stomach cold; forty pieces of cardamom to alleviate qi and help digestion; one tael of rhizome of Chinese yam; fourteen pieces of white cardamom to warm the stomach and strengthen the spleen for better appetite; four pieces of nutmeg, prepared to warm the middle and tonify the spleen, fostering digestion, not rapidly expelling like cyperus and tangerine peel. Combine into a powder, roll into pills the size of lotus seeds, take two or three pills per dose, dissolved in rice drink. One variation adds three qian of costus root.

Renshen Yangwei Decoction treats exterior wind-cold and interior cold damage, with chills and fevers like malaria, or symptoms of nausea and vomiting. The Pingwei Powder contains thick peach bark, supplemented by fragrant white atractylodes to disperse dampness from the upper jiao while tonifying the stomach; it prevents too much upward movement that could break the harmony, and is not merely a warming and tonifying formula. Ingredients: ginseng, thick peach bark (processed with ginger), and fragrant white atractylodes to induce sweating; two qian of roasted licorice; patients with weakness may adapt with cardamom; five qian each of boldo and poria to regulate stomach qi; two qian and five fen of red tangerine. Take two or three qian each time, along with three slices of ginger and one black plum, boiled in water.[76p]

　　四神丸　治脾肾禀虚，泄泻不食，或不食去后不实，或乳母患此，致儿为患。　　肉豆蔻　北五味子各二两　补骨脂四两　吴茱萸一两　　右为末，用水二碗，生姜八两，红枣一百枚，煮熟，取枣肉和末，丸麻子大，每服二三十丸，空心食前白汤下，子母并服。
　　五苓散　治藿乱吐泻，躁渴饮水，小便不利。有辰砂名辰砂五苓散。　　泽泻五钱　猪苓　官桂　赤茯　白朮各三钱　　右为末，每服一二钱，白汤调下。《幼科全书》曰：此乃分理阴阳之要药。薛己曰：按前证若津液偏渗于大肠，大便泻而小便少者，宜用此药分利。若阴阳已分而小便短少者，此脾肺气虚而不能生水也，宜用补中益气汤加麦冬、五味。虚火上炎而小便赤少者，此肺气受伤而不能生水也，用地黄丸加麦冬、五味。[77p]

Four Spirit Pill: Treats spleen and kidney deficiency, causing diarrhea and loss of appetite. It can also affect nursing mothers, leading to issues for their children.
Ingredients:

  • Nutmeg: 2 taels
  • Northern Schisandra: 2 taels
  • Psoralea: 4 taels
  • Wuzhuyu: 1 tael

Grind these into powder. Use 2 bowls of water, 8 taels of fresh ginger, and 100 red dates, boil until done. Mash the date flesh and mix with the powder, shaping into pills the size of sesame seeds. Take 20-30 pills before meals with warm clear soup, for both mother and child.

Wu Ling Powder: Treats symptoms such as violent vomiting and diarrhea, excessive thirst for water, and difficulty urinating. Known for mercury powder as Wu Ling Powder.
Ingredients:

  • Alisma: 5 qian
  • Polyporus: 3 qian
  • Cinnamon: 3 qian
  • Red poria: 3 qian
  • Atractylodes: 3 qian

Grind into powder, taking 1-2 qian mixed with warm clear soup. The "Complete Book of Pediatrics" states this is a key medicine for balancing yin and yang. Xue Ji said: If fluids are excessively seeping into the large intestine, causing diarrhea with little urination, this medicine is appropriate for unblocking. If yin and yang have been separated but urination is still scarce, this is due to spleen and lung qi deficiency affecting water generation, and it is advisable to use the Qi-boosting Decoction with added Mai Dong and Schisandra. If there is deficiency fire rising, causing reddish and scanty urination, this indicates lung qi damage and an inability to produce water, and one should use the Rehmannia Pill with added Mai Dong and Schisandra.[77p]

　　玉露散　治伤热吐泻黄色。
　　石膏煅，《幼科全书》用滑石　寒水石各五钱　甘草二钱五分　　右为末，每服五分，白汤调下。海藏曰：韭肾热相火大盛者，不宜服此。薛己曰：按前证若饮食如常，作渴饮冷，属胃经实热，宜用此药。若食少体倦，或善噫泻黄，此脾虚色陷也，宜用六君子加柴胡、升麻。若泻而变青，更兼腹胀或善怒，此脾虚肝所乘也，宜用前汤更加木香。
　　木瓜丸　治生下吐。
　　木瓜　麝香　腻粉　木香　槟榔各等分　　右为末，面糊丸黍米大，每服一二丸，甘草汤化下。薛己曰：按前证多因妊娠胃经有热，或郁痰所致，当审其母而兼治之。[78p]

Yulu San: Treats injuries from overheating, vomiting, and diarrhea with yellow fluid.

Gypsum calcined, as noted in the "Complete Book of Pediatrics," uses talc and cold water stone, each five qian, and licorice two qian and five fen. Mix these into a powder; take five fen each time, dissolving in white decoction. Haicang says: If there is excessive kidney heat and fire from the liver, do not use this. Xue Ji states: If the patient maintains a normal diet but experiences thirst for cold drinks, it indicates excessive heat in the stomach channel; this medicine is appropriate. If the patient eats little, feels fatigued, or has yellow diarrhea, it indicates spleen deficiency and requires the Six Gentlemen Decoction with Chaihu and Shengma added. If the diarrhea turns green, accompanied by abdominal distention or irritability, this suggests spleen deficiency being overrun by the liver; it is advisable to use the previous decoction with additional muxiang.

Mugua Wan: Treats vomiting during pregnancy.

Ingredients include equal parts of papaya, musk, greasy powder, mXiang, and betel nut. Grind into powder, then knead into pills the size of millet grains. Take one or two pills each time, dissolving in licorice decoction. Xue Ji notes: The preceding symptoms are often due to heat in the stomach channel from pregnancy or phlegm stagnation; one should consider the mother and treat accordingly.[78p]

　　梓朴散　小儿吐泻胃虚及有痰惊。
　　半夏汤泡七次，用生姜汁浸半日晒干，一钱　梓州厚朴一两　　右以米泔三升，同浸一百刻，水尽为度。如未尽，少加火熬干，去厚朴，只研半夏，每服半钱或一字，薄荷汤调下。
　　二气散　小儿吐泻，不拘冷热，惊吐反胃一切吐利诸治不效者。又郑氏名阴阳丸。　　硫黄半两　水银二钱半
　　右同研，不见星，每服一字至半钱，生姜水调下，其吐立止。或同炒结砂为丸。
　　二陈汤 【《幼科全书》，下同】 　治痰饮为患，或呕吐恶心，或头眩心悸，或中脘不快，或发为寒热，或因生冷伤脾。　　陈皮　半夏汤泡七次　白茯　甘草　姜三片，煎服　如呕吐加白朮、干姜煨，此二味呕吐必用之药也。如夹热而吐者，加干姜煨、黄连炒同煎。凡伤食加神曲、麦芽炒、砂仁、香附子、山楂，此五味消导必用之药也。一方加乌梅一个。[79p]

Zipu San
For children with vomiting and diarrhea, stomach deficiency, and phlegm-induced shock.
Prepare Banxia Decoction by soaking it seven times; use fresh ginger juice to soak for half a day and then dry it. Take ten grams of Zizhou Houpu (thick-skinned magnolia) and one liang (approximately 50 grams); combine this with three sheng (approximately 600 ml) of rice water, soaking for one hundred moments, reducing until the water is gone. If any remains, gently heat until dry, remove the Houpu, and grind the Banxia. Take half a qian (approximately 1.5 grams) or one word dosage, mixed in mint decoction.

Erqi San
For children with vomiting and diarrhea, regardless of hot or cold, experiencing shock and re-vomiting. Also known as Yin Yang Wan by the Zheng family.
Ingredients: 25 grams of sulfur, 5 grams of mercury.
Grind these together until no lumps remain and take one word to half a qian, mixed with ginger water. This will stop the vomiting. Alternatively, fry them together into pills.

Erchen Decoction
Treats phlegm and drink-related ailments, which may include vomiting, nausea, dizziness, palpitations, discomfort in the center of the abdomen, occurring due to cold or injuries to the spleen from raw foods.
Ingredients: Chenpi (dried tangerine peel), soaked Banxia, Bai Fu Ling (white poria), licorice, three slices of ginger, and decoct. If there is vomiting, add Baizhu (white atractylodes) and dry ginger. These two herbs are essential for treating vomiting. If accompanied by heat and vomiting, add fried dry ginger and Huanglian.
If there's food injury, add Shenchuan (fermented wheat), malt, sand ginger, Xiangfuzi (liquid ambrosia), and Hawthorn; these five herbs are essential for digestion. One recipe includes one Wu Mei (dried black plum).[79p]

Nutmeg Pill
Two qian of sand ginger, three qian of broad-leaved wood incense, seven and a half qian of red stone resin, nutmeg processed, five qian each of dried alum, white dragon bone, and haritaki pulp. Grind everything into a fine powder, make pills the size of a millet grain, and take them with aged rice soup. This medicine is warm and moist, thus it stops diarrhea.

Adjustment Decoction
Astragalus, ginseng, and licorice. Boil these in water and take them. This is the sacred medicine for treating deficiency heat. If the heat does not subside, add stir-fried dried ginger for immediate effect. If the body is hot but the hands and feet are cold, add a piece of熟附子 (prepared Aconite), and its effect is miraculous.

Response Pill
Seven grains of croton, removing the oil skin; two and a half qian of wood incense; one nutmeg; one qian each of cloves and dried ginger; seven peeled and crushed apricot kernels; and two qian of herb powder. First, grind the apricot kernels and herb powder separately into a fine powder. Boil one liang of yellow rice vinegar in a silver vessel, let it cool, then use two qian of fragrant oil to fry until cooked, mix with the vinegar to form pills, and take with mint malt soup.

Spleen Accumulation Pill
Use more green hawthorn, equal parts of cyperus, lignum nodi, purple gold peel, sand ginger, and licorice. Grind these into a fine powder. Use fresh hawthorn, pound it finely, and dry it in the sun. Make pills the size of a tung seed, and take fifty pills at a time, swallowing with drink.[80p]

True Supplement Pills

Stomach Poria Pills [from "Fragmented Jade Heart Book", same below]
Divides yin and yang, dispels tidal heat, stops vomiting and diarrhea, alleviates edema and jaundice, regulates the spleen and stomach, halts cloudy stool, commonly used for children.
Five qian each of dry white atractylodes, scraped and dried black skin soaked in rice wash water; tangerine peel; and thick bark stir-fried; roasted licorice and grass fruit two qian each; three qian each of polyporus, alisma, and white poria; one qian of cinnamon. Grind into powder, form into water pills the size of millet, take with rice soup. "Complete Book of Pediatrics" lists it as a powder, without grass fruit. For vomiting, take with ginger soup. For stomach adjustment, take with rice soup. For white turbidity, take with salted soup. For diarrhea, take with rice and plantain tea. For tidal heat, take with water bamboo leaves and rice soup. For edema, take with decoction of lamp wick and five-horned skin. For hernia, take with fennel soup. For jaundice, add five qian of gardenia and take with lamp wick tea.[81p]

A single pill of red medicine treats children's diarrhea.
Two taels of cold water stone, one tael of dried alum, grind together into a fine powder, mix with water to form pills the size of mung beans; take one pill with rice soup.

Digestive pill
To treat warm stomach and relieve diaphragm, stop vomiting, and digest milk food; when the pulse is deep, it indicates undigested food.
Use half a tael each of honey-fried licorice and aged tangerine peel, one tael each of crushed sand ginger, fried shenkui, fried cyperus, and fried barley sprout.
Grind these into a fine powder and form into pills the size of millet; for children over seven, make thirty pills the size of mung beans, to be taken with ginger soup after meals.

Another formula: for children with internal vomiting of milk or dark green stools. A lady's milk of one bowl, add ten cloves, remove one qian of aged tangerine peel, boil together until thirty boils.
Remove the cloves and tangerine peel, slightly warm, and give to the child.

Digestive pill
To treat children’s issues from coldness after drinking milk; excessive cold air accumulates in the spleen and stomach, which are the sea of grains and water. The spleen's qi grinds and digests, and when the stomach qi is harmonious, milk and food are digested; but if the spleen is damaged by cold, the food will not digest. This medicine relaxes the middle, promotes qi, digests milk food, and restores normal color.
Use half a tael each of crushed sand ginger, aged tangerine peel, fire-baked san leng, fire-baked wormwood, fried shenkui, and fried barley sprout; plus one tael of fried cyperus.
Grind these into a fine powder, make into pills the size of mung beans, and take twenty pills with perilla soup after meals.[82p]

Heji Guanyin San: For treating children suffering from external cold wind and internal injury to the spleen and stomach, resulting in vomiting, diarrhea, and refusal of milk and food, which over time leads to gradual emaciation. Generally, if the spleen is deficient, diarrhea occurs; if the stomach is deficient, vomiting occurs; if both the spleen and stomach are deficient, vomiting and diarrhea persist. This medicine is highly effective in nourishing the spleen and stomach and promoting the intake of food and drink.

Ingredients:

  • Stone lotus meat, ginseng, and fried shenqu, each 9 grams
  • Poria, 6 grams
  • Honey-fried licorice, wood fragrance, honey-fried astragalus, fried white hyacinth beans (peeled), and angelica, each 3 grams.

Grind the above into a powder. Each dose is 6 grams, mixed with one cup of water, one date, and three leaves of peppermint, decocted and taken warm.

Xiangpu San: For treating vomiting and diarrhea.

Ingredients:

  • Peppermint, dried tangerine peel, and fried magnolia bark, each 21 grams
  • Fried licorice, 6 grams
  • Half summer, soaked in decoction seven times, 30 grams.

Grind the above into a powder. Each dose is 9 grams, mixed with one cup of water, five slices of ginger, and one date, decocted for consumption. If diarrhea is severe, add wood fragrance and nutmeg.

Zhu Ru Tang: For treating stomach heat from external pathogens, causing restlessness and a preference for coolness, along with persistent vomiting.

Ingredients:

  • Kudzu root, 22.5 grams
  • Half summer, 15 grams, soaked
  • Raw licorice, 6 grams.

Mouthfully chew the above. Each dose is 9 grams, mixed with one cup of water, adding a small amount of bamboo leaf and a little ginger, decocted until reduced by one-third, then strain for clear liquid, let it cool slightly, and consume carefully at any time. An alternative addition of Poria (9 grams) enhances the effect.[83p]

　　苏合香丸　治传尸骨蒸，诸项劳瘵，顺气化痰，卒暴心痛，鬼魅疟疾，霍乱吐泻，赤白下痢，小儿惊搐。　　丁香　青木香　白檀　沉香　荜拨　香附米　诃子肉　乌犀镑肩　朱砂研水飞，各一两　熏陆香　片脑各五钱　麝香研，七钱五分　苏合香油五钱，入安息香膏内　安息香另成末用　无灰酒半升，熬膏　　右为末，用安息香膏入蜜和丸如芡实大，空心，用沸汤化下。小儿一丸，老人四丸，酒下亦可。用腊纸裹一丸弹子大，用绯绢袋盛常带之，一切邪神不敢近。去脑名麝香苏合香丸，治一切邪及胸膈噎塞，肠中虚鸣，宿食不消，余证并同。
