Suhexiang Pill

Treats corpse effusion and various labor-related diseases, regulates qi and transforms phlegm, sudden acute heart pain, ghostly ailments, malaria, cholera with vomiting and diarrhea, and children's fright and convulsions.

Ingredients:

  • Clove, 1 tael
  • Green wood fragrance, 1 tael
  • White sandalwood, 1 tael
  • Agarwood, 1 tael
  • Long pepper, 1 tael
  • Cyperus tuber, 1 tael
  • Chebulic myrobalan pulp, 1 tael
  • Black rhinoceros shoulder, 1 tael
  • Cinnabar, powdered in water, 1 tael
  • Xunlu fragrance, 5 qian
  • Borneol, 5 qian
  • Musk, powdered, 7.5 qian
  • Suhexiang oil, 5 qian, mixed into benzoin ointment

Preparation:

  • Prepare the benzoin separately in powder form.
  • Use half a sheng of ashless wine to boil and create a paste.
  • Use the mixture to form pills the size of fox nuts with a hollow center to be dissolved in boiling water.
  • Dosage: 1 pill for children, 4 pills for the elderly, can also be ingested with wine.
  • Wrap each pill in wax paper, store in a silk bag, and keep on person; all evil spirits will not dare approach.

This is called Musk Suhexiang Pill, treating all evil spirits, chest and diaphragm blockage, intestinal rumbling, indigestion, and similar ailments.

Qingzhou White Pill

Treats all types of wind-phlegm and children's convulsions.

Ingredients:

  • Fresh Tian Nanxing, 3 taels
  • Fresh Bai Fuzi, 3 taels
  • Chuan Wutou (with skin and seed removed), 3 taels
  • Fresh Banxia, 7 taels

Preparation:

  • Soak in well water, change to fresh water the next morning.
  • Dry for the following periods: spring for 5 days, summer for 3 days, autumn for 7 days, winter for 10 days, then grind into fine powder.
  • Prepare millet congee as a base and form pills the size of mung beans. For children’s convulsions, take with mint soup.
  • Combine with Suhexiang Pill for consumption, named Xiangqing Pill.[84p]

　　温胆汤　治小儿心经虚怯，夜卧不宁。　　枳实　陈皮　茯苓　生甘草　半夏泡，各等分　竹茹少许　　右銼散，白水煎，加姜二片，枣一枚，空心服。
　　紫霜丸　治食积。亦是伤寒之药。治乳哺失节，宿滞不化，胃腹痞满，呕吐恶心，便利不调，乳食减少。又治伤寒温壮挟热实，大便酸气，食不消化；或已得汗，身热不除；或变蒸发热，多日不解；或因食而发癎，先寒后热，并宜服之。　　代赭石煅，用酢淬七次　赤石脂煅，各一两　杏仁去皮尖，五十枚　巴豆三十粒，去皮膜油炒研　　右先将杏仁、巴豆入乳钵内细研如膏，却入代赭石脂研和匀，以汤浸蒸饼，丸如粟米大，一岁儿五丸，米饮下一二；百日儿三丸。亦要看肥瘦，微泻为度。大凡变蒸与伤寒调理一同，此药并治之。此药乃是泻食积之剂，要辨虚实用丸数。[85p]

Wen Dan Decoction treats the deficiency and timidity of the heart in children, causing restlessness at night. The ingredients are equal parts of: bitter orange, dried tangerine peel, Poria, raw licorice, and half-processed pinellia. A small amount of bamboo shavings is added. Grind these ingredients into a powder, then decoct in clear water. Add two slices of ginger and one jujube, and take on an empty stomach.

Zi Shuang Pill treats food accumulation and is also a remedy for cold damage. It addresses irregularities in breastfeeding, stagnation and failure to digest, stomach and abdominal fullness, nausea and vomiting, irregular bowel movements, and decreased milk intake. It also treats warm diseases with heat and full conditions leading to sour stools and indigestion; cases of sweating where body heat does not resolve; persistent heat with no relief for days; or sudden convulsions following a meal, with cold symptoms first then hot.

The ingredients include: calcined red ochre, quenched in vinegar seven times, and calcined red petroleum, each one tael; fifty peeled apricot kernels; thirty kernels of castor bean, skinned, oiled, stir-fried, and ground. First, finely grind the apricot kernels and castor beans into a paste in a mortar, then mix and grind them with the red ochre. Soak the mixture in soup to steam into cakes, shaping into pills the size of corn. For a one-year-old, five pills; for a hundred-day-old child, three pills. Dosages should also consider body condition, with slight laxative effects being ideal. Generally, this remedy for transformed heat and cold damage is treated together, and this medicine targets food accumulation, requiring differentiation of deficiency and excess for dosage.[85p]

　　香薷饮　治阴阳不顺，清浊相干，气射中焦，名为霍乱。皆由饱食豚脍，复啖乳酪，海陆百品，无所不食，多饮寒浆，眠卧冷席，风冷之气，伤于脾胃，诸食结而不消，阴阳二气壅滞不得流行，阳气欲降，阴气欲升，阴阳交错，变成吐利不已，脏腑昏乱，荣卫俱虚，冷传于筋令转筋，宜服此剂，大有神效。　　厚朴姜汁炒　香薷　白扁豆各一两，炒黄　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，酒半盏，同煎至七分，去滓，用新汲水频频浸换，令极冷顿服之，药冷则速效也。煎时不得犯铁器，慢火煎之。兼治非时吐利霍乱，腹中撮痛，大渴烦躁，四肢逆冷，汗出如雨，两脚转筋，疼痛不可忍者，须井中沉令极冷顿服之，乃有神效。治泻痢，加黄连。治霍乱吐泻，暑月感冒伤暑之证，加川芎、白芷。[86p]

Scented Mugwort Drink: It treats the imbalance of yin and yang, the interference of clear and turbid, and the qi obstructing the middle burner, known as cholera. This is all due to overindulgence in rich foods like pork and additionally consuming dairy products, eating a variety of foods from land and sea without restraint, excessive intake of cold drinks, sleeping on cold bedding, and the chilling winds causing damage to the spleen and stomach. All food gets stuck and cannot be digested, leading to stagnation of the two energies of yin and yang, where yang qi wants to descend and yin qi wants to ascend, intertwining and resulting in continuous vomiting and diarrhea, confusion in the organs, and both nutrient and protective energies being depleted. Cold invades the muscles, causing cramps. It is advisable to take this remedy, which has significant efficacy.

Recipe: Use one tael each of thick bark, ginger juice, sautéed scented mugwort, and white hyacinth bean, stir-fried until golden. Grind them together and take three qian with one cup of water and half a cup of wine, simmer until reduced to seven parts, strain, and use freshly drawn water to rinse repeatedly, making it extremely cold, then take it at once; the colder the medicine, the quicker the effect. When boiling, do not use iron utensils, and simmer slowly.

It also treats atypical vomiting and diarrhea, abdominal pain, great thirst, irritability, cold extremities, excessive sweating, and unbearable cramping in the feet. One should immerse it in well water until extremely cold before taking, for it possesses remarkable efficacy. For treating dysentery, add Huang Lian (Coptis); for cholera with vomiting and diarrhea due to summer heat, add Chuan Xiong (Szechuan lovage root) and Bai Zhu (white atractylodes).[86p]

　　理中丸　冶脾胃不和，中塞上冲胸膈，心腹逆满(疒丂)痛，痰逆恶心呕吐，心下虚烦，痞满膈塞不通，饮食减少，短气羸困，温中逐水，止汗去湿，泄泻注下，水谷不分，腹中雷鸣，伤寒时气，里寒外热，霍乱吐利，手足厥冷，胸痹心痛，逆气短气，寒多不饮水而吐。　　人参去芦　白朮　干姜炮，各三两　甘草炒，减半　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，煎六分，去滓，带热服，空心食前，或研细末白汤调下。腹痛者加人参一两半。寒多加干姜一两半。渴者加白朮一两半。脐上筑者，肾气动也，去白朮加桂四两。吐多者，去朮加生姜三两。下多者，还用朮。悸者，加茯苓二两。或四肢拘急，腹满下利转筋者，去朮加附子一个生用末之，蜜丸如鸡子黄大，名理中丸，又名调中丸。治厥除脏寒，蛔上入膈，吐长虫；或胃中虚冷，因发汗，故吐虫，先服理中丸。或加枳实、茯苓，蜜丸，治伤寒结胸欲绝，心膈高起，实满作痛，手不得近，并用热汤化下。[87p]

Li Zhong Wan treats disharmony of the spleen and stomach, obstruction in the upper body affecting the chest and diaphragm, reverse fullness and pain in the heart and abdomen, phlegm reflux leading to nausea and vomiting, mental restlessness due to deficiency below the heart, blockage and fullness in the diaphragm, reduced appetite, shortness of breath, and fatigue. It warms the center and expels water, stops sweating and removes dampness, resolves diarrhea, and distinguishes between water and food, causing roaring in the abdomen. In cases of cold damage with heat outside, cholera with vomiting and diarrhea, cold hands and feet, chest constriction and heart pain, reverse qi and shortness of breath, excessive cold leading to refusal to drink water and vomiting.

Ingredients:

  • Ginseng (prepared without the skin) 3 taels
  • White Atractylodes 3 taels
  • Dried Ginger (processed) 3 taels
  • Licorice (fried) 1.5 taels

Each dose should be ground, taken as 9 grams, boiled with 1 cup of water until reduced to 6 parts, strained, and taken warm on an empty stomach before meals, or ground into a fine powder and mixed with warm white decoction.

For abdominal pain, add 1.5 taels of ginseng. For those with excessive cold, add 1.5 taels of dried ginger. For thirst, add 1.5 taels of white atractylodes. If there is tension above the navel, this indicates kidney qi movement, remove white atractylodes and add 4 taels of cinnamon. For excessive vomiting, remove atractylodes and add 3 taels of fresh ginger. If there’s excessive diarrhea, revert to using atractylodes. For palpitations, add 2 taels of Poria.

If the limbs feel tight, the abdomen is full, and there are issues with diarrhea and cramping, remove atractylodes and add 1 piece of aconite (fresh) powdered, mixed with honey to form balls the size of egg yolks, called Li Zhong Wan, also known as Tiao Zhong Wan. It treats cold extremities and helps dispel internal cold, addresses worms moving up to the diaphragm, and may also treat a cold stomach that is weak and induces sweating, thus causing worm expulsion. It can be enhanced with bitter orange and Poria in honey balls for treating cold damage with chest fullness, heart fullness causing pain, and to warm and dissolve it with hot broth.[87p]

　　酿乳法　治初生婴儿，以表用药。凡有胎热证，当令乳母服药，不可求效之速。治法当酿乳令儿吃，渐次解之，百无一失。若遽以冷药攻之，必损脾胃；加以呕吐，必成大患。　　泽泻二两半　猪苓　赤茯　花粉各一两半　生地黄二两　茵陈　生甘草各一两　　右(口父)咀，每服五钱，水一盏，煎六分，食后捏去旧乳却服。[88p]

Brewing Milk Method: For treating newborn infants, this is a method of applying medication. If there are symptoms of fetal heat, the wet nurse should take medicine, and one must not expect quick effects. The treatment method involves brewing the milk for the child to consume, gradually resolving the issue without fail. If cold medicines are taken abruptly, it will surely harm the spleen and stomach; coupled with vomiting, it will lead to serious complications.

Ingredients:

  • 2.5 taels of ZeXie (Alisma)
  • 1.5 taels each of Pigweed (ZhuLing), Red Poria (ChiFu), and Flower Pollen (HuaFen)
  • 2 taels of Raw Rehmannia (ShengDiHuang)
  • 1 tael each of Artemisia (YinChen) and Raw Licorice (ShengGanCao)

Preparation:
Mince the above ingredients, take 5 qian of the mixture, add one bowl of water, and boil down to six portions. After meals, discard the old milk and take this preparation instead.[88p]

Ren Shen Powder: Treats children's coldness in the internal organs. If they just consumed milk and soon vomited, or if they are startled and suffer external signs such as a dark blue-black face and lips, hot soles, excessive saliva, and persistent vomiting, or have diarrhea with symptoms like blue, yellow, purple, or white, it is advisable to administer this.

White Cake: Used to treat children's food stagnation and cold illness, evidenced by fever, vomiting, and possibly abdominal pain and belching. Identify the symptoms clearly. Fermented Milk Method
Treats stomach weakness with vomiting and diarrhea, vomiting in sleep, lolling tongue and shaking head, emitting milk with a fishy smell, excessive sweating on the forehead, and excessive crying with a yellow face. For those with this illness, it is advised to temporarily stop breastfeeding to dry the stomach; if very hungry, use medicine. Let the wet nurse ferment the milk. Ingredients: Ginseng, saussurea, aromatic herbs, agarwood, dry tangerine peel, ferment for digestion, malt, each one tael; half a tael of clove.
Grind the above, take four qian, with three slices of ginger, ten leaves of perilla, and three dates to boil, then after the wet nurse eats, squeeze out all the milk, and only then take about half a cup, rest a little, and then nurse the child.[92p]

　　没石子丸　治婴孩先因冷泻，或作赤白痢候，久而变作诸般异色，不止一端，外证而或青或白，唇舌干焦，手微冷，浑身温壮，肚内刺痛啼叫，睡卧不安。　　没石子五钱　木香　黄连　当归各一两　青皮一钱　　右五件为末，阿魏一钱，酒一盏，浸化，入面少许，须令匀，煮糊为丸如粟米大，一二岁儿服如椒目大者，四五六岁儿每服五十丸。赤痢，甘草汤下；白痢，干姜汤下，或用五倍子汤下。一方用没石子一个，白豆蔻五个，诃子肉二个，木香黄连各一钱为末，梗米糊丸麻子大，每服十五丸，米饮下。
　　来复丹　治小儿虚寒泄利。
　　硝石　硫黄　太阴元精石各一两　陈皮　五灵脂　青皮各二两　　右方修制及服法俱详前。[93p]

Moshi Ziwang is used to treat infants with diarrhea caused by cold, which may present as red or white dysentery, and over time can change into various colors, with symptoms not limited to one aspect. Externally, there may be blue or white signs, with dry and scorched lips and tongue, slightly cold hands, a warm and strong body, stabbing pain in the abdomen, crying, and restless sleep.

Ingredients:

  • Moshi Ziwang: 5 qian
  • Mu Xiang: 1 liang
  • Huang Lian: 1 liang
  • Dang Gui: 1 liang
  • Qing Pi: 1 qian

Grind these five ingredients into a powder, then take 1 qian of Asafoetida, soak it in a cup of wine until dissolved. Mix a small amount into the powder until uniform, then cook until it forms a paste. Shape into pills the size of corn kernels. For children aged 1-2 years, give them pills the size of peppercorns; for children aged 4-6 years, administer 50 pills. For red dysentery, take with licorice decoction; for white dysentery, use dry ginger decoction, or administer with galls.

Another prescription suggests using 1 piece of Moshi Ziwang, 5 pieces of white cardamom, 2 pieces of haritaki fruit, and 1 qian each of Mu Xiang and Huang Lian, grind into a powder and form into pills the size of sesame seeds. Take 15 pills with rice drink.

Lai Fu Dan is used to treat children's deficiency and cold-related diarrhea.

Ingredients:

  • Nitre: 1 liang
  • Sulfur: 1 liang
  • Taiyin Yuanjing Stone: 1 liang
  • Chen Pi: 2 liang
  • Wu Ling Zhi: 2 liang
  • Qing Pi: 2 liang

The preparation and dosages for this formula are detailed above.[93p]

Silver-white powder: Treats cold diarrhea with green stools and strengthens stomach qi.
Glutinous rice and broad beans, stir-fried, each two taels; patchouli and white atractylodes, stir-fried, each one tael; cloves two qian; licorice, roasted, three qian. Mix these into powder and take with a drink of perilla seed. Add Gastrodia, cardamom, and white poria to quickly rectify the spleen. In the "Direct Instruction Formula," add roasted white fuzi, whole scorpion, wood fragrance, and stone lotus flesh, boiled with a slice of ginger.

Patchouli powder: Treats children's gastrointestinal imbalance, causing stools to be green, yellow, black, or white, with undigested milk or food. Stools may have lumps resembling frozen green egg yolks, and there may be watery diarrhea. Symptoms include slight abdominal pain and yellow-white complexion on the face and lips. If slow and alarming, or local swelling occurs, use perilla soup for three to five doses.

Add dried tangerine peel, patchouli, magnolia bark, bitter orange, stir-fried, and roasted licorice, each half a tael; mix into powder and take with three qian of perilla soup. If there are yellow-white lumps in the stool, take papaya and white plum in a salted broth. If symptoms of dysentery persist, use jujube broth. This can greatly harmonize the stomach and improve digestion for children; it is a medicine for regular use.

Da Chai Hu decoction: Treats children with heat-related diarrhea.
Chai Hu eight qian; huang qin and red peony, each three qian; half summer, soaked, one and a half qian; bitter orange, deseeded and pan-fried, half qian. Grind into powder; boil with ginger and jujubes, adjusting dosage as necessary. If needing to induce a bowel movement, add rhubarb.

Huang Lian pill: Treats children with heat-related diarrhea.[94p]

　　四逆散　治少阴病，其人或咳或悸，或小便不利，或腹中痛，或泄利下重；又治挟热泄泻尿赤。　　炙草　枳实炒黄　柴胡　白芍炒，各一两　　右捣筛为细末，水饮调下二钱，日三服。下利悸者，加桂半两。如咳者，加五味子、干姜各半两。小便不利者，加茯苓半两。泄利下重，先浓煎薤白汤，内药末三钱匕，再煮一二沸，温服。
　　调中汤　治夏月秋初，忽有暴寒折于盛暑，热结于四肢则壮热头疼，寒伤于胃则下痢赤白。　　大黄七钱半　桔梗　槁本　茯苓　生甘草　葛根　黄芩　白芍药炒　白朮各半两　　右(口父)咀，白水煎，量大小加减服之，得快气利壮便歇。去大黄，加黄连、枳谷，止痢尤妙。或加地榆，或加当归皆可。感风加荆芥。秋宜下，当用大黄疏利。[95p]

Huanglian, half a tael, purified; pig bile, soaked for two nights and dried. Flos Trichosanthis root, Wu mei flesh, almond soaked and peeled, double kernels; Shilian flesh, each half a tael. The above is ground into powder, and mixed with cow bile to form pills the size of sesame seeds. Take fifteen pills, boiling with Wu mei, ginger, and honey water.

Sijisan treats lesser yin disorders, where the patient may cough or experience palpitations, have difficulty urinating, abdominal pain, or diarrhea with heaviness; also treats heat-related diarrhea and red urine.

The ingredients: roasted licorice, fried bitter orange, Chaihu, and fried white peony, each one tael. Grind and sift into fine powder, take two qian with water and drink three times a day. For diarrhea and palpitations, add half a tael of cinnamon. If coughing, add half a tael each of Schisandra and dried ginger. For difficulty urinating, add half a tael of Poria. For diarrhea with heaviness, first use a strong decoction of Allium fistulosum, then add three qian of the powdered medicines, boiling again for one or two moments and drink warm.

Tiaozhong Decoction treats instances in summer and early autumn when a sudden cold arises amidst intense heat, causing heat to bind in the limbs resulting in fever and headache, or cold injuring the stomach leading to red and white diarrhea.

It includes: Dahuang, seven and a half qian; Platycodon, dried root; Poria; raw licorice; kudzu root; Huangqin; fried white peony; and Bai Zhu, each half a tael. Grind all, boil in plain water, adjusting dosage as necessary to achieve smooth, robust bowel movements. Remove Dahuang, adding Huanglian and Zhi Guo to stop diarrhea especially. Alternatively, add Di Yu or Dang Gui as needed. For wind, add Jing Jie. In autumn, it is appropriate to use Dahuang for relief.[95p]

　　黄芩汤　治下利而头痛胸满，口苦咽干，或往来寒热而呕，其脉浮大而弦，专治协热而利者。　　黄芩一两半，炒　白芍药炒　甘草炙，各一两　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，枣子一个，水一盏，煎至七分，去滓温服。呕者，加制半夏、生姜汁。

Huangqin Decoction: This is used to treat diarrhea accompanied by headaches and chest fullness, bitterness in the mouth, dryness in the throat, or alternating chills and fever with vomiting. The pulse is floating, large, and taut, specifically addressing heat and diarrhea. Use one and a half taels of Huangqin (Scutellaria baicalensis), one tael each of stir-fried Baishaoyao (Paeonia lactiflora), and honey-fried Gan Cao (Licorice). Crush them together, take three qian each time with one date and one cup of water, and decoct until reduced to seven parts, then discard the dregs and take warm. If there is vomiting, add prepared Banxia (Pinellia ternata) and ginger juice.

Si Shun Qingliang Drink: This treats infants with blocked blood vessels, internal heat in the organs, red cheeks, thirst, agitation of the five hearts, restless sleep, and twitching limbs; caused by irregular breastfeeding, improper temperature, leading to the child’s blood and qi being unregulated, digestive issues, scanty urination, and loose stools; or damp heat causing impending febrile diseases; or persistent heat that could lead to convulsions; and it also treats wind-heat scrofula, sores and abscesses on the face, red eyes, sore throats, and all obstructive toxins. Use one tael each of Chi Shaoyao (Red Peony), Danggui (Angelica sinensis), fresh Gan Cao, and Da Huang (Rhubarb). Crush and mix them, for children over three, take two qian each time with one cup of water, decoct until reduced to seven parts, making it into two doses. For unstoppable heat-related diarrhea, add Mu Xiang (Aucklandia) and Da Huang. If needing to promote urination, use Chi Shaoyao. For deficiency heat, add Gan Cao. If urination is difficult, reduce Da Huang. If in the presence of wind evil, add Mahuang (Ephedra) without branches. For strong body from a stroke, if the eyes look up, add Du Huo (Angelica pubescens). Adjust the dosage for the child’s size and condition, and slight diarrhea is acceptable. You can add Jing Jiao (Schizonepeta) as well. There is also a modified cooling drink that can be detailed for use.[96p]

Fragrant Orange Cake: Treats injuries and relieves cold diarrhea.

Mu Xiang (Aucklandia) and Qing Pi (Green Orange Peel) stir-fried, Chen Pi (Dried Orange Peel) each one qian (3 grams); Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) stir-fried with ginger juice, Shen Qu (Fermented Barley), Mai Ya (Barley Sprout) stir-fried, each half liang (15 grams). Full Scorpion Guanyin Powder: Stops vomiting and diarrhea, halts wind deficiencies.

Huang Qi (Astragalus), honey-roasted; Ren Shen (Ginseng), Mu Xiang, Bai Fu Ling (White Poria), roasted Da Fen Cao (Large Candy Grass), Shilia (Stone Lotus Flesh), roasted Bian Dou (Hyacinth Bean) each one liang; Bai Zhi (Angelica), and full scorpions each seven qian; Qiang Huo (Notopterygium), Fang Feng (Saposhnikovia), Tian Ma (Gastrodia) each eight qian. The right side is powdered; each dose is two qian, boiled with one cup of water until reduced to seven parts, taken with ginger and dates.

Adjusting the Middle Decoction: Treats food-induced diarrhea. Diarrhea should not be immediately supplemented; first use food medicinals or Zi Shuang Pills to eliminate accumulated matters, then supplementation can occur. The classic states: Food-based diarrhea should take precedence, for weak symptoms use supplements; a good doctor understands this principle, and there is no worry about difficult ailments.

Ren Shen, Bai Fu Ling, Bai Zhu (White Atractylodes), stir-fried Mu Xiang, roasted Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger), Huo Xiang (Agastache), Xiang Fu Zi (Cyperus) fried to remove hair, stir-fried Sha Ren (Cardamom), honey-roasted Gan Cao (Licorice), and Ding Xiang (Clove) each one liang. Jinshi Pills: Treats undigested milk and food, fullness and swelling of the heart and abdomen, strong heat and coarse breathing, vomiting phlegm, intestinal sounds and diarrhea, undigested rice and grains, possible red and white diarrhea, abdominal pain with heaviness, as well as dietary disorders like milk lumps, and blockages of qi. It also treats heat accumulation in the chest of children, stagnant fluids in the abdomen causing blockage of qi in the organs, leading to abdominal distension and possible strong heat. Anyone with these ailments should promote bowel movements to disperse qi and consistently take this remedy.

Ingredients:

  • 1 qian Ba Dou powder
  • Soaked and dried Ai Ye (Angelica) mixed and roasted
  • Zhu Sha (Cinnabar)
  • Dai Zhe Shi (hematite) calcined and processed seven times
  • Zhi Ke (Bitter Orange) roasted
  • Mu Xiang (Costus)
  • Each in five qian
  • 1 fen of She Xiang (Musk)

The above ingredients are ground into a fine powder, shaped into pills the size of sesame seeds. For a one-year-old child, administer one pill with warm water, adjusting dosage based on their condition. Take after meals to treat food accumulation causing heat, weakness, distended abdomen, and abdominal pain during breastfeeding.

Sheng Jiang Xie Xin Decoction: Used for treating cold disorders with sweating, resolving disharmony in the stomach, hardness below the heart, water in the sides, and thunderous sounds in the abdomen with diarrhea.

Ingredients:

  • 1.5 liang Huang Lian (Coptis)
  • 1.5 liang Zhi Cao (Liquorice)
  • 1.5 liang Ren Shen (Ginseng)
  • 1.5 liang Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger)
  • 1.5 liang Huang Qin (Scutellaria)
  • 1 liang Ban Xia (Pinellia), soaked and washed

Grind the above ingredients, take three qian of this mixture, combine with a cup of water, three slices of fresh ginger, and one date. Boil down to three-quarters, discard the residue, and take warm.

Bao An Pills: Treats diarrhea from food retention and damage from improper eating in children.[98p]

Sanling pills treat children's accumulated heat and fullness in the abdomen and sides, causing dry vomiting and nausea, preventing food intake. Xing Shuang pills treat children's food accumulation leading to diarrhea and dysentery.

Three taels of Xingren, shelled and stir-fried; one tael of Badu, oil removed and slightly charred; yellow wax and wine boiled and strained; Baicao powder ground, with six qian of oil stir-fried, each two taels. For red dysentery, swallow with licorice soup; for white dysentery, with ginger soup. Begin with three to four doses; for abdominal bloating, ten or more doses, and it is remarkably effective.[99p]

　　至圣保命丹　治小儿胎惊内吊，腹肚紧硬，眠睡不安，夜多啼哭；及治急慢惊风，眼目上视，手足抽掣，不省人事，悉皆主之。冷证用此。　　全蝎十四个，去毒　防风二钱　僵蚕炒去丝嘴　天麻　南星炮　蝉蜕　白附各二钱　麝五分　金箔十片　朱砂二钱　　右为末，粳米糊丸，每两作四十丸。常服镇心安神化痰，除一切惊风诸证，汤临时换。一方加人参、白茯苓各二钱。有热证，加牛黄一分，冰片一分，硼砂一钱。
　　钓藤散　治小儿夜啼，乃脏冷也。阴盛于夜则冷动，冷动则为阴极发躁，寒盛作疼，所以夜啼不歇也，钓藤散主之。　　钓藤钩　茯神　川芎　当归酒洗　茯苓　木香　甘草炙　白芍药炒，各一钱　　右为末，每服一钱。姜、枣略煎服。其或心热而烦啼，必有脸红舌白小便赤濇之候，钓藤饮去木香加朱砂末一钱研和，每服一钱，木通汤调下，或銼散煎服。治惊啼，加蝉蜕、防风、天麻。[100p]

Zhi Sheng Bao Ming Dan treats children suffering from fright due to the fetus, presenting with a tight and hard abdomen, restless sleep, and frequent crying at night; it also addresses sudden or chronic convulsions, with symptoms like upward gaze, convulsive limbs, and loss of consciousness. This remedy is effective for cold patterns.

Ingredients:

  • 14 pieces of whole scorpion, detoxified
  • 2 qian of Fang Feng
  • 2 qian of silkworm, fried and depilated
  • Tian Ma
  • Nuan Xing, processed
  • Cicada slough
  • 2 qian each of Bai Fu
  • 0.5 qian of musk
  • 10 pieces of gold leaf
  • 2 qian of cinnabar

Grind the above into a powder, mix with glutinous rice paste to make pills, 40 pills per two liang. Regular consumption calms the heart, stabilizes the spirit, transforms phlegm, and alleviates all kinds of convulsions; preparation of a decoction is seasonal. In one variation, add 2 qian each of ginseng and white poria. For heat patterns, add 0.1 qian of buffalo horn, 0.1 qian of borneol, and 1 qian of borax.

Diao Teng San treats children’s night crying, which indicates internal cold. When yin prevails at night, it causes cold movement; this agitation can lead to pain, resulting in incessant night crying—Diao Teng San addresses this.

Ingredients:

  • Diao Teng (Uncaria)
  • Fu Shen
  • Chuan Xiong
  • Dang Gui, washed in wine
  • Fu Ling
  • Mu Xiang
  • Zhi Gan Cao
  • Bai Shao Yao, fried, each 1 qian

Grind together, and take 1 qian per dose, boiled with ginger and jujube. If there is heart heat causing restless crying, look for signs of a red face, white tongue, and reddish urine. Use Diao Teng Yin, adding 1 qian of cinnabar powder mixed in, taken with Mu Tong decoction or made into a powder for decoction. For frightful crying, add cicada slough, Fang Feng, and Tian Ma.[100p]

Dingming Yinzi – For the treatment of slow reactions, shock, vomiting, diarrhea, and heaviness. It is intended for slow spleen usage.
Ingredients: 1. Banxia (Pinellia) 2. Fuling (Poria) 3. Muxiang (Aucklandia) 4. Old ginger, sliced and dried 5. Baizhu (Atractylodes), fried – each 2 qian. 6. Gancao (Licorice), roasted – 1 qian. 7. Tianma (Gastrodia) – 2.5 qian.

Zhujun San – For the aftermath of vomiting and diarrhea, particularly when there is a greenish stool; it is advisable to take this.
Ingredients: 1. Renshen (Ginseng) 2. Baizhu, fried 3. Bai Fuling (White Poria) 4. Gancao, roasted – each 1 liang. 5. Chensha (Cinnabar), processed with water – 0.5 liang. 6. Diaoteng (Uncaria) – 0.5 liang. 7. Dengxin (Lampwick) – 3 qian. 8. Shexiang (Musk) – 0.5 qian.
Grind into powder, and take 1 qian with white soup, without timing restrictions.

Suijing Taiyi Dan – Regular use calms the spirit, alleviates fright, and stops night crying with greenish stools.
Ingredients: 1. Jiegeng (Platycodon) – 1 liang, fried. 2. Huo Xiang (Agastache) – 0.5 liang. 3. Biandou (Lablab Bean) – 0.5 liang, fried. 4. Baizhi (Angelica) – 3 qian. 5. Chuanxiong (Ligusticum) – 3 qian.

Appetizer Pills

This remedy treats children with weak internal organs, suffering from wind and coldness, abdominal distention, intestinal rumbling, diarrhea (possibly green or white), and indigestion from milk or food; it also addresses cold internal organ night crying and abdominal pain from cold during pregnancy.

Ingredients:

  • Mu Xiang (Costus Root) and E Zhu (Zedoary) – each 1.5 taels
  • Bai Zhu (Atractylodes) and Ren Shen (Ginseng), and cooked Dang Gui (Angelica) – each 0.5 taels
  • She Xiang (Musk), finely ground – 0.1 tael
  • Bai Shao (White Peony) – 0.1 tael

Preparation:
Grind the above ingredients into a fine powder. Soak them in broth to make pills the size of millet. Take 15 pills with warm rice drink. For newborns with abdominal pain and night crying, five pills may be taken before breastfeeding.

Hou Po San (Magnolia Bark Powder)

This remedy treats children with disharmony between the spleen and stomach, leading to persistent diarrhea, emaciation, and poor appetite.

Ingredients:

  • Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) – outer rough skin removed, coated with ginger juice, roasted until aromatic
  • Ren Shen (Ginseng) – 0.1 tael
  • He Li (Amomum) – roasted with skin
  • Bai Zhu (Atractylodes) – 0.1 tael
  • Chuan Huang Lian (Chinese Goldthread) – trimmed and lightly roasted
  • Di Yu (Sanguisorba) – slightly roasted – 0.1 tael
  • Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice) and Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger) – each 0.5 tael
  • One piece of Mu Guo (Nutmeg), shell removed

Preparation:
Grind the above into a fine powder. For each dose, take half a penny of the powder with porridge drink, three to four times a day, adjusting the dosage according to the child's size.[102p]

Zhang Huan's Houpo San for treating diarrhea.

Wanquan Longgu Wan for treating children’s imbalanced cold and heat, occurring with diarrhea that doesn't stop.

Liu’s formula for treating children’s diarrhea.

Xiangju Bing for treating infants overindulging in milk or food, leading to either vomiting or diarrhea; also for recovery from illness where they feel weak, have a dull expression, and show sallow complexion.

Zhang Huan's E Jiao Dan: It treats heat from excessive urination and sudden diarrhea. The ingredients are: 1 tael of true E Jiao, 1 tael of dry ginger, half a tael each of peony root, angelica root (washed and roasted), Sichuan huanglian, and nutmeg. Shen Xian Yu Fen Dan: It nourishes all deficiencies without causing heat, especially effective for children with cold accumulation and sudden diarrhea. The main ingredient is one pound of refined sulfur from merchant ships, crushed to remove sand and stones.

Use seven hog stomachs and three pounds of white mulberry root; chop the root into pieces. Clean the hog stomachs thoroughly, stuff them with sulfur, and sew them shut with hemp twine. Add 20 quarts of water, boiling one pound of white mulberry root first, then simmer the remaining hog stomachs slowly without letting them cool. After one boil, switch out the hog stomachs, boiling with another pound of white mulberry root, repeating this process for three boils. After the third boil, only replace the hog stomachs, boiling a total of seven times. Replenish the water with hot broth, avoiding cold water. Once boiled seven times, remove and rinse with warm water, grinding into a very fine powder. Sun-dry it thoroughly in the strong sunlight and grind again. Form the mixture into pills the size of a phoenix seed, taking ten to fifteen pills with warm millet drink on an empty stomach. This greatly eliminates residual cold and is highly effective. It can be used by the elderly for a long time.

Infant Dragon Bone Decoction: Treats children's persistent diarrhea. Ingredients: calcined dragon bone, roasted Gan Cao, Sichuan Huanglian each four fen; Danggui, dry ginger each one fen. Combine with four sheng of water, boil down to one sheng and two ge, and take three doses warm before meals. This can also address diarrhea that continues after taking medicine.[107p]

　　龙骨五分　甘草炙　干姜　当归　黄连　附子炮制去皮脐　赤石脂　前胡各三分　　右以水四升，煮一升二合，为五服，旦服至午令尽。
　　黄连煎　治冷热利经久不止，体羸不堪，治瘥而又发。　　好黄连二两，水七升，蜜八合，煎一升三合　　右绞去滓，百日儿半合，二百日、一岁服一合。
　　鸡骨丸　治下利经久不断，羸瘦，脾胃冷弱，食不消化。　　宿雌鸡胸前及肋骨全用一具　黄连六分　厚朴三分　神曲炒　甘草炙　白朮各四分　桔梗　麦芽炒　乌梅各二分　人参　赤石脂　黄芩　白龙骨各五分　　右为末，蜜丸小豆大，白饮下二十五丸，日二服，量儿大小与之。
　　惺惺散　治久泻脾困，不思乳食，恐作脾风。　　天麻　全蝎炒，各半钱　木香炮　糯米　人参　白茯苓各炒微黄　白扁豆炒　干山药焙　甘草各一钱，炙　　右为末，每服婴孺一字，二三岁半钱，用水一药注，或半银盏，枣子半片，煎十数沸服。[108p]

Ingredients:

  • Dragon bone: 5 parts
  • Licorice (fried): 3 parts
  • Dried ginger: 3 parts
  • Angelica: 3 parts
  • Coptis: 3 parts
  • Prepared aconite (peeled): 3 parts
  • Red earth resin: 3 parts
  • Fritillaria: 3 parts

Preparation:
Boil 4 liters of water until it reduces to 1.2 liters, to make 5 doses, to be taken daily until noon.

Coptis Decoction:
Treats persistent issues of hot and cold, particularly for those who are weak and unable to bear it, aiding recovery but also causing recurrence. Use 200 grams of good coptis, 7 liters of water, and 800 grams of honey, boil down to 1.3 liters. Strain to remove dregs, and take half a cup for a child aged 100 days, and adjust the dosage for 200 days or 1 year accordingly.

Chicken Bone Pills:
Treats continuous diarrhea, weakness, a cold and weak spleen and stomach, and poor digestion. Use the entire breast and ribs of a broody hen, 60 grams of coptis, 30 grams of magnolia bark, 40 grams each of fried malt, licorice (fried), and white atractylodes, 20 grams each of platycodon, roasted barley, and black plum, 50 grams each of ginseng, red earth resin, scutellaria, and white dragon bone. Grind to a fine powder, make honey pills the size of a soybean, take 25 pills with warm water, twice a day, adjusting for the size of the child.

Awakening Powder:
Treats long-term diarrhea due to spleen deficiency, lack of appetite for milk and food, with concerns of inducing spleen wind. Use equal parts of Tianma and whole scorpion (fried), and half a qian each of benzoin; stir-fried glutinous rice, ginseng, white poria; one qian each of fried hyacinth bean, baked yam, and licorice (fried). Grind to powder, and give children aged 2-3 half a qian of this mix, mixed with water or half a silver cup, and decoct until boiling for several moments before consumption.[108p]

　　香矾丹　张涣治泻利久不瘥。
　　南木香　枯白矾各一两　诃梨勒皮微炮　酸石榴皮炒黑，各半两　　右件捣罗为细末，炼蜜和丸如黍米大，每服十粒，粥饮下，量儿大小加减。
　　刘氏方　治小儿脏腑久泻不止。
　　人参　白朮　茯苓　甘草　陈皮　藿香　丁香　木香　肉豆蔻　　右等分为末，每服二钱，以藿香合糯米煮粥饮调下，或姜水煎亦可。脏腑滑泄，四君子加诃子五分，米饮调下。
　　圣惠厚朴散　治小儿水谷利，羸瘦面黄，不欲饮食。　　厚朴去粗皮涂生姜汁炙令香熟　龙骨　丁香　黄连去须微炒，各半两　当归銼微炒　木香　白朮　肉豆蔻各一分　　右件药捣，细罗为散，每服以粥饮下半钱，日三四服，量儿大小加减。
　　地榆散　治水谷利，日夜不止。
　　地榆炙　厚朴去粗皮涂姜汁炙令香热，各三分　黄连一两，去须微炒　阿胶半两捣碎炒令黄色　　右件药捣，细罗为散，不计时候，以粥饮调下半钱，量儿大小加减。[109p]

Xiang Fan Dan: By Zhang Huan, used for treating prolonged diarrhea that does not heal.

Ingredients:

  • Southwood fragrance, dried white alum, each one tael
  • Cold pear skin, slightly roasted
  • Sour pomegranate skin, roasted until black, each half a tael

Method: Crush and sift the above into a fine powder, refine with honey, and form into pills the size of millet grains. Take ten pills each time, consumed with congee, adjusting the dosage according to the child's size.

Liu's Formula: For treating prolonged diarrhea in young children.

Ingredients:

  • Ginseng
  • White Atractylodes
  • Poria
  • Licorice
  • Dried tangerine peel
  • Patchouli
  • Cloves
  • Wood fragrance
  • Nutmeg

Method: Equal parts of the above, ground into powder. Take two qian each time, mix with patchouli and glutinous rice to make congee, or decoct with ginger water. If the intestines are slippery, add five fen of hezi (a type of fruit) and mix with rice drink.

Sheng Hui Hou Po San: For treating children with watery stools, emaciation, pale complexion, and lack of appetite.

Ingredients:

  • Hou Po (Magnolia Bark), remove rough skin and roast with ginger juice until fragrant
  • Dragon bone
  • Cloves
  • Coptis, remove the beard and lightly roast, each half a tael
  • Angelica, finely chopped and lightly roasted
  • Wood fragrance
  • White Atractylodes
  • Nutmeg, each one fen

Method: Crush the above medicines and sift into powder. Take half a qian mixed with congee three to four times a day, adjusting the dosage according to the child's size.

Di Yu San: For treating watery stools that do not cease day and night.

Ingredients:

  • Roasted Di Yu (Sanguisorba)
  • Hou Po, with rough skin removed and roasted with ginger juice until fragrant, each three fen
  • Coptis, one tael, remove the beard and lightly roast
  • Ejiao (Donkey-hide gelatin), half a tael, crushed and roasted until yellow

Method: Crush the above into powder and sift. Take half a qian mixed with congee at any time, adjusting the dosage according to the child's size.[109p]

　　胃风汤　治风冷乘虚，入客肠胃，水谷不化，泄泻注下，腹胁满，肠鸣(疒丂)痛，及肠胃湿毒，下如豆汁，或下瘀血，日夜无度，并宜服之。　　人参　白茯苓　芎藭　桂皮去粗皮　当归　白芍药　白朮各等分　　右为粗散，每服二钱，以水一大盏，入粟米百粒，同煎七分，去滓稍热服，空心食前服，小儿量减。
　　三神丸　养生治大小老虚之人，不拘冷热泄泻。　　黄连　白芍药并銼如豆　吴茱萸各十两　　右三味，釜内慢火炒赤色，放冷，杵罗为细末，每服三钱匕，水一盏半，煎至八九分，去滓，空腹食前温服，日三四服，小儿量与。或以水浸蒸饼，丸如桐子大，更丸一等如菉豆黄米大，小儿每服十五丸至二十丸，温米饮下。若作散，以沸汤或温米饮调下，并可服。病泄痢之人，若不禁生冷鱼肉肥腻，与不服药同。一方有木香无芍药，酢糊丸。[110p]

Stomach Wind Decoction - It treats the invasion of wind and cold into the empty channels, causing disturbances in the intestines and stomach, leading to undigested food, diarrhea, fullness in the abdomen and sides, intestinal rumbling, pain, and damp-heat toxins in the intestines, which may discharge like bean juice or old blood, with constant urgency day and night. It is advisable to take this.

Ingredients: ginseng, white poria, cyperus, cinnamon (remove coarse skin), angelica, white peony, and atractylodes, all in equal parts.

The above is ground coarsely. Each dose consists of two qian (a traditional weight unit), to be boiled with one large cup of water and one hundred grains of millet until reduced to seven parts. Strain and take it warm before meals on an empty stomach, adjusting the dosage for children.

Three Divine Pills - Nourishes and treats the elderly or deficient individuals, regardless of heat or cold-related diarrhea.

Ingredients: coptis, white peony (both ground like beans), and evodia, each ten liang (a larger weight unit).

These three ingredients are roasted slowly over fire until reddish, then cooled and ground into a fine powder. Each dose is three qian, taken with one and a half cups of water, boiled down to eight or nine parts, strained and taken warm before meals on an empty stomach, three to four times a day, adjusting for children. Alternatively, water can be used to soak thin cakes, formed into pills the size of a nut, with another batch the size of a yellow soybean. Children may take fifteen to twenty pills, washed down with warm rice drink. If made as a powder, it can be mixed with boiling water or warm rice drink and taken. Those with diarrhea or dysentery should refrain from consuming raw, cold, or fatty meats, similar to how they would take the medicine. There is a variant that includes wood fragrant without peony, called vinegar paste pills.[110p]

　　茅先生香连丸　治泻痢。
　　黄连茱萸半两，同于铫内炒令烟起，取出去茱萸　木香　肉蔻　诃子炮去核，各五钱　阿胶面炒　朱砂各一钱　　右为细末，软饭为丸如桐子大，每服十丸十四丸，用饭饮吞下，儿小碎之。
　　乳香散　治一切泻痢。
　　乳香二钱，荷叶盛火炙令令熔，放地上碗盖另研　肉豆蔻　白姜　甘草炙　草果各一两　　右细銼，用酢面裹，于热灰内，煨令赤色，取出去面为末，入乳香拌匀，每服五分或一钱，陈米饮调下。
　　守中汤　春夏相交，阴湿气重，中伤脾胃，致腹痛泄痢，经久不止，渐传手足浮肿，饮食少思。　　苍朮泔水浸一宿，去粗皮滤干，銼，炒微黄色　桔梗各二两，炒　白姜四钱，炮　甘草六钱，炙　　右件銼，焙为末，每服一钱，空心沸汤调服，(口父)咀水煎亦可，或用姜、枣。[111p]

Mr. Mao's Xiang Lian Wan treats diarrhea and dysentery.

Mix half a tael of huanglian and zhuyou, fry together in a pan until smoke rises, then remove the zhuyou. Take five qian each of muxiang, roukou, and hezi (removing the seeds), and one qian each of ejiao flour and zhush, grind them into fine powder. Form into pills the size of apricot seeds using soft rice, taking ten to fourteen pills with rice wine. For children, crush them.

Ruxiang San treats all kinds of diarrhea and dysentery.

Use two qian of ruxiang, roast it on a hot lotus leaf until it melts, then place it in a bowl on the ground. Grind together one liang each of rou doukou, bai jiang, gan cao (roasted), and cao guo. Slowly grind until fine, wrap in a mixture of vinegar and flour, and bake in hot ash until red. Remove the flour, grind into powder, mix with ruxiang, taking five fen or one qian at a time, diluted with aged rice wine.

Shou Zhong Tang is used when spring and summer overlap, bringing heavy dampness that harms the spleen and stomach, leading to abdominal pain and persistent diarrhea, which can eventually cause swelling in the hands and feet, and a decrease in appetite.

Soak cangzhu in water overnight, remove the rough skin, filter dry, grind and lightly fry until slightly yellow; use two liang of jiegeng, fry; four qian of bai jiang, and six qian of gan cao (roasted). Grind the combined ingredients into fine powder, taking one qian in empty stomach with hot soup, or you can take it in water boiled with ginger and jujube.[111p]

　　张涣川椒丸　治小儿夏伤湿冷入肠胃，泄泻不止。　　川椒一两，去闭目双者并黑子，慢火炒香熟为度　肉豆蔻五钱　　右件捣罗为细末，粳米饭和圆如黍米大，每服十粒，米饮下，量儿大小加减。

　　温中汤　治胃寒泻白，腹痛肠鸣，孔氏治脏腑不调，大便青色。　　白朮　人参　茯苓各一钱　甘草炙，半钱　　右末一钱，水一小盏，煎七分，温服。
　　黄芩汤　治下痢而头痛胸满，口苦咽干，或往来寒热而呕、其脉浮大而弦者，或协热而痢者。　　黄芩一两半　芍药　甘草炙，各一两　　右銼散，每服三钱，枣子一个，水一盏，煎七分，去滓温服。呕者加半夏一两二钱半，生姜煎。[112p]

Zhang Huan's Chuan Jiao Pill treats children suffering from summer-related cold dampness affecting the stomach and intestines, causing persistent diarrhea.

Ingredients: One tael of Chuan Jiao, with black seeds and closed eyes removed, roasted over a slow fire until fragrant and cooked. Five qian of nutmeg.

These ingredients are to be ground into a fine powder, mixed with glutinous rice, shaped into round pills about the size of a millet grain. Take ten pills with rice drink, adjusting the dosage based on the child's size.

Sorghum Decoction treats intestinal issues caused by wind and cold, leading to persistent diarrhea and a strong body heat.

Ingredients: One tael each of white atractylodes, angelica, Chuan xiong, ginseng, cinnamon, and peony.

These ingredients are to be ground into a fine powder, with each dose being one qian, mixed with a small cup of water, three slices of ginger, and a spoonful of millet, boiled down to five parts, with the millet cooked, strained, and taken warm.

Warming Middle Decoction treats cold-induced white diarrhea, abdominal pain, intestinal sounds, and issues with the internal organs, resulting in greenish stools.

Ingredients: One qian each of white atractylodes, ginseng, and poria; half a qian of roasted licorice.

The powdered mixture is one qian, boiled with a small cup of water, and taken warm after reducing to seven parts.

Huang Qin Decoction treats dysentery accompanied by headache, chest fullness, bitter mouth, dry throat, or alternating chills and fever with vomiting, often showing a floating, wiry pulse, or heat-related dysentery.

Ingredients: One and a half taels of huang qin, one tael each of peony and roasted licorice.

These are to be ground into a fine powder. Each dose is three qian, cooked with one jujube and a cup of water, boiled down to seven parts, strained and taken warm. If there is vomiting, add one and a half taels of pinellia and cook with ginger.[112p]

小儿吐泻门

　　　　单方

　　治小儿霍乱吐利：用人参一两，厚朴、甘草各半两，白朮十八铢[白朮十八铢　原缺，据《千全》卷五癖结胀满补。]，四味(口父)咀，以水一升二合，煮取半升，六十日儿服一合，百日儿分三服，期岁分二服，中间隔乳服之。乳母忌生冷油腻等。一加干姜一分，或加生姜三分。　　【《千全方》，下同】[113p]

Zhang Huan's Qingwei Powder treats heat-induced diarrhea.

Ingredients:

  • 1.5 grams of Prickly Ash Fruit
  • 1.5 grams of Huangbai (Coptis) lightly roasted
  • 1.5 grams of Angelica, washed and baked
  • 1.5 grams of Ground Euyin (Earth Elm), roasted
  • 1.5 grams of Huanglian (Coptis), stems removed and stir-fried

Grind these ingredients into a fine powder. For each dose, take 3 grams, mix with 240 ml of water, and boil down to 60 ml. Strain and take warm before dairy intake.

Xianglian Pill:
Stir-fry Huanglian with ginger juice, 60 grams, and blend it with 15 grams of Mu Xiang. Form into pills the size of a mung bean with cooked rice; take 10-20 pills with rice drink; alternatively, mix with Liu Yi Powder.

For children's vomiting and diarrhea: For treating pediatric cholera with vomiting and diarrhea, use 30 grams of Ginseng, 15 grams each of Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) and Licorice, 18 grams of Bai Zhu (Atractylodes). Chew these ingredients together, add 2.4 liters of water, and simmer to obtain 600 ml. For infants under 60 days old, give 20 ml; for those over 100 days, divide into three doses; for one-year-olds, give two doses, separating each from dairy intake. Nursing mothers should avoid raw, cold, and greasy foods. Optionally, one can add 3 grams of dried ginger or 9 grams of fresh ginger.[113p]

　　小儿霍乱：梳头垢水服少许。

　　治孩子霍乱，已用立验：用人参、芦箨各半两[各半两　原缺，据《千金》卷五癖结胀满补。]，扁豆藤二两，仓米一撮，四味(口父)咀，以水二升，煮取八合，分温服。　　又方用：人参一两[一两：原缺，据《千全》卷五癖结胀满补。]，木瓜一枚，仓米一撮，三味(口父)咀，以水煮分服，以意量之，立效。
　　治小儿霍乱：研尿滓，乳上服之。
　　又：以牛涎灌口中一合。

　　治少小吐利：用乱发半两烧灰，鹿角六铢，二味为末，米汁服一刀圭，日三服。　　又方：热牛屎含之。一作牛膝。
　　又方：烧牡猪屎，水浸取汁，少少服之。
　　治小儿哕：用生姜汁、牛乳各五合，煎取五合，分为二服。　　又方：取牛乳一斤，煎取五合，分五服。[114p]

For childhood cholera: use a small amount of water from washing hair.

To treat children's cholera, proven effective: use half a liang of both ginseng and reed leaves, two liang of adzuki bean vine, a pinch of wet rice, chew these four ingredients, boil in two sheng of water, and take eight (he) in warm doses. Another method: one liang of ginseng, one piece of papaya, a pinch of wet rice, chew these three ingredients, boil in water and divide according to need; it will have immediate effect.

To treat young children’s diarrhea: grind urine residue and give it with milk.

Additionally: use cow bile to wash in the mouth in a small quantity.

To treat slight vomiting and diarrhea: use half a liang of burnt hair ash, six zhu of deer antler, grind these two into powder, and take a spoonful with rice juice three times a day. Another method: hold hot cow dung in the mouth. Some say cow's knee instead.

Another method: burn wild boar dung, soak in water to extract juice, and take a little of it.

To treat young children's hiccups: mix five sheng of fresh ginger juice with five sheng of cow's milk, boil to reduce to five sheng, and divide into two doses. Another method: take one jin of cow's milk, boil to reduce to five sheng, and divide into five doses.[114p]

　　小儿脾泄不止：红枣二十个去核，将官粉入内，以阴阳瓦焙干，去枣研粉，每服三分，米汤下。
　　小儿饮乳后吐逆不入腹：取芦蠹虫二枚，煮汁饮之。呕逆与哯乳不同，乳饱后哯出者，为哯乳也。【藏器方】
　　小儿吐泻，脾胃虚寒：齐州半夏泡七次，陈粟米各一钱半，姜十片，水盏半，煎八分，温服。【《直诀》】
　　治泻不止：用笋箨、扁豆藤各半两，人参一两，共细銼，分六服，每水一小盏，煎五分，不时量分，稍热服。【《圣惠方》，下同】
　　小儿吐乳：取地龙粪一两研末，空心，米泔汤服效。
　　凡小儿霍乱吐泻：用土蜂窠炙研，乳汁服一钱。
　　小儿百晬内吐乳，或粪青色：用年少妇人乳汁一盏，入丁香十枚，陈皮一钱，石器煎一二十沸，细细与服。【陈文仲小儿方】
　　小儿吐泻，巴豆一个，针穿灯上烧过，黄蜡一豆大，灯上烧滴入水中，同杵丸黍米大，每用五七丸，莲子灯心汤下。【危氏《得效方》】[115p]

  1. For a child with continuous diarrhea due to spleen deficiency: Take twenty dried red dates, remove the pits, and fill them with official powder. Bake them dry using a yin-yang tile, then grind the dates into a powder. Take three grams of this powder with rice soup.

  2. For a child who vomits after drinking milk and is unable to keep it down: Take two larvae of the bamboo beetle, boil them to extract the juice and drink it. Vomiting differs from spitting up; if a child expels milk after being full, it is considered spitting up.

  3. For a child with vomiting and diarrhea due to weak and cold spleen and stomach: Soak Qizhou pinellia seven times, add one and a half qian of aged glutinous rice, and ten slices of ginger, with half a cup of water. Boil until reduced to one-fifth, then take warm.

  4. For treating persistent diarrhea: Use half a liang of bamboo shoots and broad bean vines, and one liang of ginseng. Grind finely and divide into six doses. Boil each dose in a small cup of water for five minutes, then take while warm.

  5. For a child vomiting milk: Take one liang of earthworm feces and grind it into a powder. Take it on an empty stomach with rice rinse water.

  6. For all children with cholera-like vomiting and diarrhea: Use ground soil bee nests, roast and grind, and take one qian mixed with milk.

  7. For a child vomiting milk or with greenish stools: Use one cup of milk from a young mother, add ten cloves and one qian of dried tangerine peel. Simmer in a stone vessel until it reaches boiling, then administer carefully.

  8. For vomiting and diarrhea in children: Use one areca nut that has been pierced and roasted over a lamp, add a bean-sized amount of yellow wax, and drip it into water. Form into pills the size of millet, and take five to seven pills with lotus seed and lampwick soup.[115p]

　　寡妇槁荐草节，去小儿霍乱。 【《酉阳杂俎》】
　　襁褓吐乳欬嗽久不愈：石燕子为末，以蜜调少许涂唇上，日三五次。 【《卫生宝鉴》】
　　小儿吐泻：芹菜切细，煮汁饮之，不拘多少。 【《子母秘录》】
　　小儿呕吐不止：丁香、生半夏各一钱，姜汁浸一夜，晒干为末，姜汁打面糊丸黍米大，量大小用姜汤下。【《全幼心鉴》，下同】
　　小儿哯乳：用咸豉七个去皮，腻粉一钱同研，丸黍大，每服三五丸，藿香汤下。

  1. A widow uses dried grass to soothe a child's cholera.
  2. For infants who cough and have not recovered for a long time: grind stone swallow into powder, mix with a little honey, and apply to the lips three to five times a day.
  3. For children with vomiting and diarrhea: finely chop celery, boil it to extract juice, and have them drink it without restriction.
  4. For children who vomit persistently: take one penny each of cloves and raw pinellia, soak in ginger juice overnight, then dry and grind into powder. Make into pills the size of millet grains, and administer with ginger soup according to size.
  5. For children regurgitating milk: take seven salted fermented soybeans, remove the skin, and grind with one penny of greasy powder into pills the size of millet grains; take three to five pills with hoelen soup.

　　又治泄泻：用车前子不拘多少为细末，每服二钱，米饮汤调下服之，水谷分，吐泻止。

For treating diarrhea: Use caraway seeds, ground finely in any amount, taking two qian with rice soup to swallow; this separates food and water, stopping vomiting and diarrhea.

　　小儿吐逆不止，用黄丹研末，小枣肉和丸芡子大，每以一丸针签于灯上烧过研细，乳汁调下。一加朱砂、枯矾等分。【谢氏小儿方】

　　小儿疳泻：赤石脂末，米饮调服半钱，立瘥。加京芎等分更妙。

Childhood malnutrition and diarrhea: Grind half a qian of red stone powder and mix it with rice drink to take; it will heal immediately. Adding an equal part of ligusticum is even better.

Childhood nausea and vomiting, wind-related wheezing: Grind equal parts of white atractylodes and patchouli into powder, and take half a qian with rice drink.

Childhood irregular vomiting: Use two pieces of galla, one cooked and one raw, one handful of licorice, moistened with paper and roasted, grind together into powder; take half a qian with rice wash for immediate relief.

Childhood heat diarrhea: Peel and roast phellodendron to a fine powder and mix it into small balls with rice soup; take one or twenty balls with rice soup.

Childhood seasonal diarrhea: Use three parts of prepared white atractylodes, aged tangerine peel, and Sichuan magnolia bark, and stir-fry them with ginger juice; add two parts of licorice. For vomiting, add four parts of patchouli leaves; for body heat and abdominal pain, add three parts of fried yellow root with ginger water.

Childhood diarrhea: Take one piece of jujube, wrap it in flour and steam, remove the shell, and grind three pieces of small cloves into powder; place the powder into the child’s navel and seal it with an old plaster.

Childhood prolonged diarrhea, poor appetite, and thin body: Equal parts of roasted white atractylodes and white poria, with a pinch of aged rice to cook porridge, only drink rice soup, and the diarrhea will cease.[119p]

　　又健脾止泻：用陈米锅巴四两，莲肉去心微炒四两，享糖四两，共研细末，食远或空心调服数匙妙。
　　小儿吐乳：苏叶、甘草、滑石各一钱，水煎服。 【《幼幼近编》，下同】
　　小儿久泻：用肉豆蔻平开，入麝香一分，再合面包煨为末，米汤下。溏泄用柿饼烧熟吃立止。身热作泻，四君子汤加白芷、黄芪、松花、五味子。
　　小儿吐泻：用干姜、甘草各二钱，炙白朮一两为末，温汤服。吐泻不止，或以白朮一钱，肉果、丁香各五分，姜汤调下，兼治大人吐泻。或以白芷、干姜为末，蜜丸置脐中，以绢缚定，用热鞋底时时熨之。

  • For strengthening the spleen and stopping diarrhea: Use four taels of aged rice crust, four taels of lotus meat (with the core removed and lightly roasted), and four taels of sugar; grind into a fine powder and take a few spoonfuls with water on an empty stomach or away from meals.
  • For infants vomiting milk: Use one qian each of suye (perilla leaves), licorice, and talc; decoct in water and take.
  • For prolonged diarrhea in children: Use nutmeg ground finely, add one fen of musk, and mix with bread to form a powder; take with rice soup. For loose stools, cook and eat persimmon cake to stop it immediately. If the body is hot with diarrhea, use Si Jun Zi decoction added with white angelica, astragalus, pine pollen, and schisandra.
  • For vomiting and diarrhea in children: Use two qian each of dried ginger and licorice, and one liang of roasted white atractylodes, powdered; take with warm water. If vomiting and diarrhea persist, use one qian of white atractylodes, five fen each of nutmeg and clove, and take with ginger soup, which can also treat adults. Additionally, powder white angelica and dried ginger, form into honey pills, place them on the navel secured with gauze, and apply warmth with a hot shoe sole to soothe.
  • For treating prolonged diarrhea that won't stop: Stir-fry equal parts of white atractylodes and white poria, and cook a pinch of aged rice into porridge; only drink the rice broth.
  • For treating prolonged vomiting that won't stop: Fry one liang of cardamom in children's urine three to four times, use one qian of clove, and three qian of patchouli; take one spoonful mixed with ginger soup.
  • For treating persistent vomiting and diarrhea in children: Use two pieces of gallnut, half raw and half cooked, grind licorice into powder, and take with five fen of rice wash water.[120p]

　　　　针灸

　　《古今医统》曰：小儿呕吐乳汁，灸中庭一穴一壮，在膻中穴下一寸陷中。
　　　　医案

　　钱乙《小儿直诀》曰：广亲官五太尉病吐泻不止，米谷不化，众医用温药一日而加喘吐不定。钱氏曰：当以凉药治之。所以然者，谓伤热在内也。用石膏汤三服并服之。众医皆言吐泻多而米谷又不化，当补脾，何以用凉药？王信众医，皆用补脾丁香散三服。钱医后至曰：不可服此。三日后，必腹满身热，饮水吐逆。三日外果如所言。所以然者，谓六月热甚，伏入腹中，而令引饮伤脾胃，即大吐泻也。众又行温药，使上焦亦热，故喘而引饮，三日当甚。众师不能治，复召钱至，见其热证，以白虎汤三服，更以白饼子下之，一日减药二分，二日三日又与白虎汤各二服，四日用石膏汤一服；及旋合门冬、黄苓、脑子、牛黄、天竺黄、茯苓，以朱砂为衣，服五丸，竹叶汤化下，热退而安。[121p]

Acupuncture

"The Comprehensive Medical Text" states: For children who vomit breast milk, moxibustion should be applied to the Zhongting point, located one inch below the Xuanji point.

Medical Case

Qian Yi in "Children's Direct Principle" states: A certain official, the Grand Marshall, is suffering from persistent vomiting and diarrhea with undigested grains. Various physicians used warming herbs but after one day, the condition worsened with irregular vomiting and shortness of breath. Qian argued that it should be treated with cooling herbs, as the heat was internal. He prescribed three doses of gypsum decoction all at once. Others said the vomiting and diarrhea were severe and the grains were not digesting, so they recommended tonifying the spleen and questioned the use of cooling herbs. Wang Xin and many other physicians used a spleen-tonifying mixture of clove powder, giving three doses. When Qian arrived later, he said that this was inappropriate. He predicted that after three days, the patient would experience abdominal fullness and a rise in body heat with water-induced vomiting. After three days, this indeed occurred. The reasoning was that during June, internal heat was intense and when it penetrated the abdomen, it caused harm to the spleen and stomach, resulting in severe vomiting and diarrhea. The others then continued using warming herbs, further heating the upper body, leading to shortness of breath and an increased urge to drink, which would worsen after three days. Unable to resolve the issue, the physicians called Qian again. Upon observing the signs of heat, he prescribed three doses of Bai Hu decoction and additionally administered Bai Bingzi. On the first day, he reduced the dosage by two fen, on the second and third days he provided two doses of Bai Hu decoction, and on the fourth day, he used one dose of gypsum decoction. He combined Lian Dong, Huang Qing, Nao Zi, Niu Huang, Tian Zhu Huang, and Fu Ling, coated with Zhu Sha, and used five pills dissolved in bamboo leaf decoction. This reduced the heat and stabilized the patient.[121p]

　　广亲宫七太尉七岁病吐泻，是时七月，其证不食而昏睡，睡觉而闷乱，哽气干呕，大便或有或无，不渴，众医作惊治之，疑睡故也。钱曰：先补脾，后退热。与使君子丸补脾，石膏汤退热；又以水银、硫黄末研和，以姜水调下一字。钱曰：凡吐泻五月内，九分下而一分补；八月内，九分补而十分下。此者是脾虚泻，医妄治之，至于虚损，下之即死，即当补脾，若以使君子丸恐缓，已又留温胃益脾药治之。医者李生曰：何食而哕？钱曰：脾虚津少即呕逆。曰：何泻青褐水？曰：肠胃至虚，冷极故也。钱治而愈。[122p]

In the Guangqin Palace, the seventh Grand Commandant, aged seven, suffered from vomiting and diarrhea. It was July at the time, and the symptoms included lack of appetite, faintness, disturbed sleep, choking sensations, and retching. The bowel movements were infrequent, and there was no thirst. Various doctors treated it as a case of shock, suspecting it was due to the sleep. Qian said: "First nourish the spleen, then clear the heat." He prescribed Shijunzi pills to nourish the spleen and gypsum decoction to clear the heat; he also ground mercury and sulfur into a powder, mixed it, and adjusted it with ginger water for administration. Qian commented: "In cases of vomiting and diarrhea, within five days, nine parts should be purged and one part nourished; within eight days, nine parts should be nourished and one part purged." He stated that this was due to a deficiency in the spleen causing diarrhea, and if the physician treated it incorrectly, it could result in death from excessive purging. Therefore, it was necessary to nourish the spleen. If using Shijunzi pills was too slow, then it must also include warming the stomach and strengthening the spleen. A physician named Li asked: "What caused the vomiting?" Qian responded: "A deficiency in the spleen and a lack of fluids leads to reverse qi." Li asked: "What caused the diarrhea of greenish-brown water?" Qian replied: "The intestines and stomach are extremely deficient, leading to severe cold." Qian treated the condition, and the patient recovered.[122p]

　　冯承务子五岁，吐泻壮热，不思饮贪，目睛多白，面色无神。师曰：此肾经虚弱，下之则愈虚。遂以消积丸磨之，渐愈。大凡伤食不下则成癖，下后即与补脾，无不效者。
　　《儒门事亲》曰：河间刘光济之子，才二岁病疱，后呕吐发昏，用丁香、豆蔻之类不效，通麻先生寄其家，乃谓光济曰：今有小方，无毒，人皆知之，公肯从乎？光济曰：先生之言，必中于理，何敢不从！麻先生曰：刘河间常言凉膈散可治疮疱，张戴人用之如神，况《内经》言少阳所至呕涌，少阳者相火也，非寒也。光济欣而从之。此日利二行，适王德秀自外入，闻其利之也，乃曰：疮疱首尾不可下。麻自悔其多言也，业已然，姑待之。比至食时，下黄涎一合，日午问之，儿已索游于街矣。
　　《保婴金镜录》曰：一小儿五岁，食粽后咬牙欲吐，顷间腹胀昏愦，鼻青黄赤，此脾土伤而心肝所动，食积发厥也。先令鸡翎探吐出酸物，顿醒。节其饮食，勿药而愈。[123p]

At five years old, Feng Chengwu's child suffered from severe vomiting and diarrhea, with high fever, lack of desire for food, and prominent whites of the eyes, looking lifeless. The teacher said: "This indicates weakness in the kidney meridian; if purged, it will only worsen the deficiency." Therefore, he ground up a digestive pill for treatment, and the child gradually recovered. In general, if food is not expelled, it leads to accumulation; after purging, then give supplements to the spleen, and efficacy is assured.

The "Confucian Door on Caring for Parents" states: Liu Guangji's son from Hejian fell ill with sores at just two years of age, later experiencing vomiting and confusion. Treatments using cloves and cardamom were ineffective. Master Ma sent to his home and said to Guangji: "Now there is a small formula, non-toxic, known by all. Will you accept it?" Guangji replied: "Surely, your words must have merit; how dare I refuse!" Master Ma continued: "Liu Hejian often says that Liangge Powder can treat sores; Zhang Dairen used it with miraculous results. Moreover, the Inner Canon states that minor yang leads to vomiting—minor yang is heat, not cold." Guangji was delighted and agreed. On that day, Li Erxing came in from outside, heard about the effectiveness, and remarked: "Sores and blisters should not be purged at the onset." Master Ma regretted his excessive words, but since it had already been done, waited patiently. As mealtime approached, the child expelled a significant amount of yellow phlegm, and by noon, when asked, the child had already gone out to play in the streets.

The "Baoying Jinjinglu" states: A five-year-old child, after eating zongzi, began to grind his teeth and wanted to vomit. Soon, he experienced abdominal distension and confusion, with a bluish yellow complexion. This indicated damage to the spleen and earth element, affecting the heart and liver, resulting in food accumulation causing convulsions. First, the child was given chicken feather to induce vomiting of sour substances, and he quickly regained consciousness. His diet was adjusted, and recovery occurred without the need for medicine.[123p]

　　薛氏《保婴撮要》曰：一小儿夏月吐乳，手指发热，作渴饮冷，口吐涎水。余谓胃气热，廉泉开而涎出也，用泻黄散而愈。后复呕吐，另用克滞之剂，口渴饮汤，流涎不已。余谓胃气虚寒不能摄涎也，用理中丸而愈。
　　一小儿七岁，呕吐不食，面白指冷，此胃气虚寒也，用理中汤，呕吐顿愈，又用六君子汤而痊。后伤食腹痛，发热呕吐流涎，先用保和丸一服而痛呕愈，再用四君、山栀而涎止。

　　一小儿伤食发热，呕吐酸物，手指常冷，此胃气虚寒，阴盛隔阳于外，虚热所致也。用保和丸末二钱，浓姜汤调服而吐止；再用六君子汤加山栀而安。[124p]
